Utah Code Annotated - Title 80 - Utah Juvenile Code
===================================================

Utah Code Annotated - Title 80 - Chapter 1 - General Provisions
***************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102 Juvenile Code definitions.
---------------------------------------------------------
Except as provided in SectionUtah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1): 76-5-308.5; 76-2-401
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(a): 76-5-308.5 "Abuse" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(a)(i): 76-5-308.5
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(a)(i)(A): nonaccidental harm of a child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(a)(i)(B): threatened harm of a child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(a)(i)(C): sexual exploitation;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(a)(i)(D): sexual abuse; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(a)(i)(E): 76-5-308.5 human trafficking of a child in violation of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(a)(ii): that a child's natural parent:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(a)(ii)(A): intentionally, knowingly, or recklessly causes the death of another parent of the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(a)(ii)(B): is identified by a law enforcement agency as the primary suspect in an investigation for intentionally, knowingly, or recklessly causing the death of another parent of the child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(a)(ii)(C): is being prosecuted for or has been convicted of intentionally, knowingly, or recklessly causing the death of another parent of the child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(b): 76-2-401 "Abuse" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(b)(i): reasonable discipline or management of a child, including withholding privileges;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(b)(ii): 76-2-401 conduct described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(b)(iii): the use of reasonable and necessary physical restraint or force on a child:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(b)(iii)(A): in self-defense;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(b)(iii)(B): in defense of others;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(b)(iii)(C): to protect the child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(1)(b)(iii)(D): to remove a weapon in the possession of a child for any of the reasons described in Subsections (1)(b)(iii)(A) through (C).
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(2): "Abused child" means a child who has been subjected to abuse.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(3): 80-6-306; 80-6-306; 80-6-402
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(3)(a): 80-6-306 "Adjudication" means, except as provided in Subsection (3)(b):
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(3)(a)(i): 80-6-306 for a delinquency petition or criminal information under Chapter 6, Juvenile Justice:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(3)(a)(i)(A): a finding by the juvenile court that the facts alleged in a delinquency petition or criminal information alleging that a minor committed an offense have been proved;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(3)(a)(i)(B): 80-6-306 an admission by a minor in the juvenile court as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(3)(a)(i)(C): a plea of no contest by minor in the juvenile court; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(3)(a)(ii): for all other proceedings under this title, a finding by the juvenile court that the facts alleged in the petition have been proved.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(3)(b): 80-6-306; 80-6-402 "Adjudication" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(3)(b)(i): 80-6-306 an admission by a minor described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(3)(b)(ii): 80-6-402 a finding of not competent to proceed in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(4)(a): "Adult" means an individual who is 18 years old or older.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(4)(b): "Adult" does not include an individual:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(4)(b)(i): who is 18 years old or older; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(4)(b)(ii): who is a minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(5): 78A-2-801 "Attorney guardian ad litem" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(6): "Board" means the Board of  Juvenile Court Judges.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(7): 80-2-905 "Child" means, except as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(8): 80-3-307 "Child and family plan" means a written agreement between a child's parents or guardian and the Division of Child and Family Services as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(9): 26B-2-101 "Child placing" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(10): 26B-2-101 "Child-placing agency" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(11): "Child protection team" means a team consisting of:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(11)(a): the child welfare caseworker assigned to the case;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(11)(b): if applicable, the child welfare caseworker who made the decision to remove the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(11)(c): a representative of the school or school district where the child attends school;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(11)(d): if applicable, the law enforcement officer who removed the child from the home;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(11)(e): a representative of the appropriate Children's Justice Center, if one is established within the county where the child resides;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(11)(f): if appropriate, and known to the division, a therapist or counselor who is familiar with the child's circumstances;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(11)(g): if appropriate, a representative of law enforcement selected by the chief of police or sheriff in the city or county where the child resides; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(11)(h): any other individuals determined appropriate and necessary by the team coordinator and chair.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(12): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(12)(a): "Chronic abuse" means repeated or patterned abuse.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(12)(b): "Chronic abuse" does not mean an isolated incident of abuse.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(13): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(13)(a): "Chronic neglect" means repeated or patterned neglect.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(13)(b): "Chronic neglect" does not mean an isolated incident of neglect.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(14): 58-37d-3 "Clandestine laboratory operation" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(15): "Commit" or "committed" means, unless specified otherwise:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(15)(a): with respect to a child, to transfer legal custody; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(15)(b): with respect to a minor who is at least 18 years old, to transfer custody.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(16): "Community-based program" means a nonsecure residential or nonresidential program, designated to supervise and rehabilitate juvenile offenders, that prioritizes the least restrictive setting, consistent with public safety, and operated by or under contract with the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(17): 80-5-402 "Community placement" means placement of a minor in a community-based program described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(18): 64-13-1 "Correctional facility" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(18)(a): a county jail; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(18)(b): 64-13-1 a secure correctional facility as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(19): "Criminogenic risk factors" means evidence-based factors that are associated with a minor's likelihood of reoffending.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(20): 26B-1-201 "Department" means the Department of Health and Human Services created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(21): "Dependent child" or "dependency" means a child who is without proper care through no fault of the child's parent,  guardian, or custodian.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(22): "Deprivation of custody" means transfer of legal custody by the juvenile court from a parent or a previous custodian to another person, agency, or institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(23): "Detention" means home detention or secure detention.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(24): 80-5-501 "Detention facility" means a facility, established by the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(25): 80-5-203 "Detention risk assessment tool" means an evidence-based tool established under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(25)(a): assesses a minor's risk of failing to appear in court or reoffending before adjudication; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(25)(b): is designed to assist in making a determination of whether a minor shall be held in detention.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(26): "Developmental immaturity" means incomplete development in one or more domains that manifests as a functional limitation in the minor's present ability to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(26)(a): consult with counsel with a reasonable degree of rational understanding; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(26)(b): have a rational as well as factual understanding of the proceedings.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(27): 80-3-405; 80-4-305 "Disposition" means an order by a juvenile court, after the adjudication of a minor, under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(28): 53G-6-202 "Educational neglect" means that, after receiving a notice of compulsory education violation under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(29): 26B-5-104 "Educational series" means an evidence-based instructional series:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(29)(a): 26B-5-104 obtained at a substance abuse program that is approved by the Division of Integrated Healthcare in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(29)(b): designed to prevent substance use or the onset of a mental health disorder.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(30): 80-7-102 "Emancipated" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(31): "Evidence-based" means a program or practice that has had multiple randomized control studies or a meta-analysis demonstrating that the program or practice is effective for a specific population or has been rated as effective by a standardized program evaluation tool.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(32): 77-15-2 "Forensic evaluator" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(33): 80-6-607 "Formal probation" means a minor is:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(33)(a): supervised in the community by, and reports to, a juvenile probation officer or an agency designated by the juvenile court; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(33)(b): 80-6-607 subject to return to the juvenile court in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(34): "Group rehabilitation therapy" means psychological and social counseling of one or more individuals in the group, depending upon the recommendation of the therapist.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(35): "Guardian" means a person appointed by a court to make decisions regarding a minor, including the authority to consent to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(35)(a): marriage;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(35)(b): enlistment in the armed forces;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(35)(c): major medical, surgical, or psychiatric treatment; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(35)(d): legal custody, if legal custody is not vested in another individual, agency, or institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(36): 78A-2-801 "Guardian ad litem" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(37): "Harm" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(37)(a): physical or developmental injury or damage;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(37)(b): emotional damage that results in a serious impairment in the child's growth, development, behavior, or psychological functioning;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(37)(c): sexual abuse; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(37)(d): sexual exploitation.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(38): 78A-6-353; 80-6-704 "Home detention" means placement of a minor:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(38)(a): if prior to a disposition, in the minor's home, or in a surrogate home with the consent of the minor's parent, guardian, or custodian, under terms and conditions established by the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services or the juvenile court; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(38)(b): 78A-6-353; 80-6-704 if after a disposition, and in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(39): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(39)(a): "Incest" means engaging in sexual intercourse with an individual whom the perpetrator knows to be the perpetrator's ancestor, descendant, brother, sister, uncle, aunt, nephew, niece, or first cousin.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(39)(b): "Incest" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(39)(b)(i): blood relationships of the whole or half blood, regardless of whether the relationship is legally recognized;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(39)(b)(ii): relationships of parent and child by adoption; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(39)(b)(iii): relationships of stepparent and stepchild while the marriage creating the relationship of a stepparent and stepchild exists.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(40): "Indian child" means the same as that term is defined in 25 U.S.C. Sec. 1903.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(41): "Indian tribe" means the same as that term is defined in 25 U.S.C. Sec. 1903.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(42): 78B-22-102 "Indigent defense service provider" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(43): 78B-22-102 "Indigent defense services" means the same as that term is defined in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(45): 80-6-607
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(45)(a): 80-6-607 "Intake probation" means a minor is:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(45)(a)(i): monitored by a juvenile probation officer; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(45)(a)(ii): 80-6-607 subject to return to the juvenile court in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(45)(b): "Intake probation" does not include formal probation.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(46): "Intellectual disability" means a significant subaverage general intellectual functioning existing concurrently with deficits in adaptive behavior that constitutes a substantial limitation to the individual's ability to function in society.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(47): "Juvenile offender" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(47)(a): a serious youth offender; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(47)(b): a youth offender.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(48): 78A-6-205 "Juvenile probation officer" means a probation officer appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(49): 80-6-201 "Juvenile receiving center" means a nonsecure, nonresidential program established by the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services, or under contract with the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services, that is responsible for minors taken into temporary custody under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(50): "Legal custody" means a relationship embodying:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(50)(a): the right to physical custody  of the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(50)(b): the right and duty to protect, train, and discipline the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(50)(c): the duty to provide the minor with food, clothing, shelter, education, and ordinary medical care;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(50)(d): the right to determine where and with whom the minor shall live; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(50)(e): the right, in an emergency, to authorize surgery or other extraordinary  care.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(51): 80-2-1002 "Licensing Information System" means the Licensing Information System maintained by the Division of Child and Family Services under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(52): 80-2-1001 "Management Information System" means the Management Information System developed by the Division of Child and Family Services under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(53): "Mental illness" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(53)(a): a psychiatric disorder that substantially impairs an individual's mental, emotional, behavioral, or related functioning; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(53)(b): the same as that term is defined in:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(53)(b)(i): the current edition of the Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders published by the American Psychiatric Association; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(53)(b)(ii): the current edition of the International Statistical Classification of Diseases and Related Health Problems.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(54): 80-6-501; 80-6-901; 80-7-102; 78A-6-103; 78A-6-103 "Minor" means, except as provided in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(54)(a): a child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(54)(b): 78A-6-103; 78A-6-103 an individual:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(54)(b)(i): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(54)(b)(i)(A): who is at least 18 years old and younger than 21 years old; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(54)(b)(i)(B): for whom the Division of Child and Family Services has been specifically ordered by the juvenile court to provide services because the individual was an abused, neglected, or dependent child or because the individual was adjudicated for an offense;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(54)(b)(ii): 78A-6-103
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(54)(b)(ii)(A): who is at least 18 years old and younger than 25 years old; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(54)(b)(ii)(B): 78A-6-103 whose case is under the jurisdiction of the juvenile court in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(54)(b)(iii): 78A-6-103

Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(54)(b)(iii)(B): 78A-6-103 whose case is under the jurisdiction of the juvenile court in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(55): 26B-5-101 "Mobile crisis outreach team" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(56): 76-5-401.1 "Molestation" means that an individual, with the intent to arouse or gratify the sexual desire of any individual, touches the anus, buttocks, pubic area, or genitalia of any child, or the breast of a female child, or takes indecent liberties with a child as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(57): 80-3-302
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(57)(a): 80-3-302 "Natural parent" means, except as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(57)(b): "Natural parent" includes the minor's noncustodial parent.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58): 78B-24-203; 80-3-304; 76-10-2202
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(a): 78B-24-203 "Neglect" means action or inaction causing:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(a)(i): abandonment of a child, except as provided in Chapter 4, Part 5, Safe Relinquishment of a Newborn Child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(a)(ii): lack of proper parental care of a child by reason of the fault or habits of the parent, guardian, or custodian;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(a)(iii): failure or refusal of a parent, guardian, or custodian to provide proper or necessary subsistence or medical care, or any other care necessary for the child's health, safety, morals, or well-being;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(a)(iv): a child to be at risk of being neglected or abused because another child in the same home is neglected or abused;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(a)(v): 78B-24-203 abandonment of a child through an unregulated child custody transfer under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(a)(vi): educational neglect.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(b): 80-3-304; 76-10-2202 "Neglect" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(b)(i): a parent or guardian legitimately practicing religious beliefs and who, for that reason, does not provide specified medical treatment for a child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(b)(ii): a health care decision made for a child by the child's parent or guardian, unless the state or other party to a proceeding shows, by clear and convincing evidence, that the health care decision is not reasonable and informed;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(b)(iii): 80-3-304 a parent or guardian exercising the right described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(b)(iv): 76-10-2202 permitting a child, whose basic needs are met and who is of sufficient age and maturity to avoid harm or unreasonable risk of harm, to engage in independent activities, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(b)(iv)(A): traveling to and from school, including by walking, running, or bicycling;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(b)(iv)(B): traveling to and from nearby commercial or recreational facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(b)(iv)(C): engaging in outdoor play;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(b)(iv)(D): 76-10-2202 remaining in a vehicle unattended, except under the conditions described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(b)(iv)(E): remaining at home unattended; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(58)(b)(iv)(F): engaging in a similar independent activity.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(59): "Neglected child" means a child who has been subjected to neglect.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(60): 80-6-701 "Nonjudicial adjustment" means closure of the case by the assigned juvenile probation officer, without an adjudication of the minor's case under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(60)(a): the assigned juvenile probation officer; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(60)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(60)(b)(i): the minor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(60)(b)(ii): the minor and the minor's parent, guardian, or custodian.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(61): "Not competent to proceed" means that a minor, due to a mental illness, intellectual disability or related condition, or developmental immaturity, lacks the ability to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(61)(a): understand the nature of the proceedings against the minor or of the potential disposition for the offense charged; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(61)(b): consult with counsel and participate in the proceedings against the minor with a reasonable degree of rational understanding.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(62): "Parole" means a conditional release of a juvenile offender from residency in secure care to live outside of secure care under the supervision of the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services, or another person designated by the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(63): "Physical abuse" means abuse that results in physical injury or damage to a child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(64): 80-6-701
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(64)(a): 80-6-701 "Probation" means a legal status created by court order, following an adjudication under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(64)(b): "Probation" includes intake probation or formal probation.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(65): "Prosecuting attorney" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(65)(a): the attorney general and any assistant attorney general;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(65)(b): any district attorney or deputy district attorney;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(65)(c): any county attorney or assistant county attorney; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(65)(d): any other attorney authorized to commence an action on behalf of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(66): 80-3-301 "Protective custody" means the shelter of a child by the Division of Child and Family Services from the time the child is removed from the home until the earlier of:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(66)(a): 80-3-301 the day on which the shelter hearing is held under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(66)(b): the day on which the child is returned home.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(67): "Protective services" means expedited services that are provided:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(67)(a): in response to evidence of neglect, abuse, or dependency of a child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(67)(b): to a cohabitant who is neglecting or abusing a child, in order to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(67)(b)(i): help the cohabitant develop recognition of the cohabitant's duty of care and of the causes of neglect or abuse; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(67)(b)(ii): strengthen the cohabitant's ability to provide safe and acceptable care; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(67)(c): in cases where the child's welfare is endangered:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(67)(c)(i): to bring the situation to the attention of the appropriate juvenile court and law enforcement agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(67)(c)(ii): to cause a protective order to be issued for the protection of the child, when appropriate; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(67)(c)(iii): to protect the child from the circumstances that endanger the child's welfare including, when appropriate:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(67)(c)(iii)(A): removal from the child's home;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(67)(c)(iii)(B): placement in substitute care; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(67)(c)(iii)(C): petitioning the court for termination of parental rights.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(68): "Protective supervision" means a legal status created by court order, following an adjudication on the ground of abuse, neglect, or dependency, whereby:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(68)(a): the minor is permitted to remain in the minor's home; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(68)(b): supervision and assistance to correct the abuse, neglect, or dependency is provided by an agency designated by the juvenile court.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(69): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(69)(a): "Related condition" means a condition that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(69)(a)(i): is found to be closely related to intellectual disability;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(69)(a)(ii): results in impairment of general intellectual functioning or adaptive behavior similar to that of an intellectually disabled individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(69)(a)(iii): is likely to continue indefinitely; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(69)(a)(iv): constitutes a substantial limitation to the individual's ability to function in society.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(69)(b): "Related condition" does not include mental illness, psychiatric impairment, or serious emotional or behavioral disturbance.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(70): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(70)(a): "Residual parental rights and duties" means the rights and duties remaining with a parent after legal custody or guardianship, or both, have been vested in another person or agency, including:

Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(96): "Validated risk and needs assessment" means an evidence-based tool that assesses a minor's risk of reoffending and a minor's criminogenic needs.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-102(97): "Without merit" means a finding at the completion of an investigation by the Division of Child and Family Services, or a judicial finding, that the alleged abuse, neglect, or dependency did not occur, or that the alleged perpetrator was not responsible for the abuse, neglect, or dependency.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-103 Cooperation of political subdivisions and public or private agencies and organizations.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-103(1): Every county, municipality, and school district, and the Department of Health and Human Services, the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services, the Division of Child and Family Services, the Office of Substance Use and Mental Health, the State Board of Education, and state and local law enforcement officers, shall render all assistance and cooperation within their jurisdiction and power to further the provisions of this title.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-1-103(2): A juvenile court is authorized to seek the cooperation of all agencies and organizations, public or private, whose objective is the protection or aid of minors.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(1): "Consult" means an interaction between two persons in which the initiating person:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(1)(a): provides information to another person;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(1)(b): provides the other person an opportunity to respond; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(1)(c): takes the other person's response, if any, into consideration.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(2): "Consumer" means a person who receives services offered by the division in accordance with this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(3): 80-2-1101 "Council" means the Child Welfare Improvement Council created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(4): "Custody," with regard to the division, means the custody of a minor in the division as of the date of disposition.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(5): "Day-care services" means care of a child for a portion of the day which is less than 24 hours:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(5)(a): in the child's own home by a responsible individual; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(5)(b): outside of the child's home in a:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(5)(b)(i): day-care center;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(5)(b)(ii): family group home; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(5)(b)(iii): family child care home.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(6): 80-2-202 "Director" means the director of the division appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(7): 80-2-201 "Division" means the Division of Child and Family Services created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(8): 77-36-1 "Domestic violence" means the same as that term is defined in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(12)(b): "Person responsible for the child's care" includes a person responsible for the child's care in the same home as the child, a relative's home, a group, family, or day care facility, a foster care home, or a residential institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-102(13): "Shelter care" means the temporary care of a minor in a nonsecure facility.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-201 Creation of division.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-201(1): There is created the Division of Child and Family Services within the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-201(2): The division is under the administration and general supervision of the executive director of the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-201(3): Chapter 2a, Removal and Protective Custody of a Child The division has all functions, powers, duties, rights, and responsibilities described in this chapter and


Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-202 Division director -- Qualifications -- Responsibilities.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-202(1): The executive director of the department shall appoint the director of the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-202(2): The director shall have a bachelor's degree from an accredited university or college, be experienced in administration, and be knowledgeable in the areas of child and family services, including child protective services, family preservation, and foster care.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-202(3): The director is the administrative head of the division.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308 Division responsibility for normalizing lives of children -- Requirements for caregiver decision making.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(1)(a): "Activity" means an extracurricular, enrichment, or social activity.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(1)(b): "Age-appropriate" means a type of activity that is generally accepted as suitable for a child of the same age or level of maturity, based on the development of cognitive, emotional, physical, and behavioral capacity that is typical for the child's age or age group.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(1)(c): "Caregiver" means a person with whom a child is placed in an out-of-home placement.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(1)(d): "Out-of-home placement" means the placement of a child in the division's custody outside of the child's home, including placement in a foster home, a residential treatment program, proctor care, or with kin.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(1)(e): "Reasonable and prudent parent standard" means the standard characterized by careful and sensible parental decisions to maintain a child's health, safety, and best interest while at the same time encouraging the child's emotional and developmental growth.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(2): Chapter 2a, Removal and Protective Custody of a Child; Chapter 3, Abuse, Neglect, and Dependency Proceedings A child who comes into protective custody or the division's temporary custody or custody under this chapter,
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(3): The division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(3)(a): make efforts to normalize the life of a child in protective custody or the division's temporary custody or custody and to empower a caregiver to approve or disapprove a child's participation in activities based on the caregiver's own assessment using a reasonable and prudent parent standard, without prior approval of the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(3)(b): allow a caregiver to make important decisions, similar to the decisions that a parent is entitled to make, regarding the child's participation in activities.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(4)(a): A caregiver shall use a reasonable and prudent parent standard in determining whether to permit a child to participate in an activity.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(4)(b): A caregiver shall consider:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(4)(b)(i): the child's age, maturity, and developmental level to maintain the overall health and safety of the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(4)(b)(ii): potential risk factors and the appropriateness of the activity;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(4)(b)(iii): the best interest of the child based on the caregiver's knowledge of the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(4)(b)(iv): the importance of encouraging the child's emotional and developmental growth;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(4)(b)(v): the importance of providing the child with the most family-like living experience possible; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(4)(b)(vi): the behavioral history of the child and the child's ability to safely participate in the proposed activity.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(4)(c): The division shall verify that a private agency providing out-of-home placement under contract with the division:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(4)(c)(i): promotes and protects the ability of a child to participate in age-appropriate activities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(4)(c)(ii): implements policies consistent with this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(4)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(4)(d)(i): A caregiver is not liable for harm caused to a child in an out-of-home placement if the child participates in an activity approved by the caregiver and the caregiver acted in accordance with a reasonable and prudent parent standard.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(4)(d)(ii): This section does not remove or limit any existing liability protection afforded by statute.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-308(5): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402 Child welfare training coordinator -- Mandatory education and training of child welfare caseworkers -- Development of curriculum.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(1): There is created within the division a full-time position of a child welfare training coordinator.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(2): The child welfare training coordinator is not responsible for direct casework services or the supervision of casework services, but is required to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(2)(a): develop child welfare curriculum that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(2)(a)(i): is current and effective, consistent with the division's mission and purpose for child welfare; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(2)(a)(ii): utilizes curriculum and resources from a variety of sources including those from:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(2)(a)(ii)(A): the public sector;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(2)(a)(ii)(B): the private sector; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(2)(a)(ii)(C): inside and outside of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(2)(b): recruit, select, and supervise child welfare trainers;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(2)(c): develop a statewide training program, including a budget and identification of sources of funding to support that training;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(2)(d): evaluate the efficacy of training in improving job performance;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(2)(e): assist child protective services and foster care workers in developing and fulfilling their individual training plans;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(2)(f): monitor staff compliance with division training requirements and individual training plans; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(2)(g): expand the collaboration between the division and schools of social work within institutions of higher education in developing child welfare services curriculum, and in providing and evaluating training.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(3): The director shall, with the assistance of the child welfare training coordinator, establish and ensure child welfare caseworker competency regarding a core curriculum for child welfare services that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(3)(a): is driven by child safety and family well-being;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(3)(b): emphasizes child and family voice;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(3)(c): is based on a policy, procedure, program, or practice that demonstrates an ability to minimize retraumatization associated with the criminal and juvenile justice system; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(3)(d): is consistent with national child welfare practice standards.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(4): 80-2-403 A child welfare caseworker shall complete training in:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(4)(a): the legal duties of a child welfare caseworker;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(4)(b): 80-2-403 the responsibility of a child welfare caseworker to protect the safety and legal rights of children, parents, and families at all stages of a case, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(4)(b)(i): initial contact;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(4)(b)(ii): 80-2-403 safety and risk assessment, as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(4)(b)(iii): intervention;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(4)(c): recognizing situations involving:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(4)(c)(i): substance abuse;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(4)(c)(ii): domestic violence;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(4)(c)(iii): abuse; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(4)(c)(iv): neglect; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(4)(d): the relationship of the Fourth and Fourteenth Amendments of the Constitution of the United States to the child welfare caseworker's job, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(4)(d)(i): search and seizure of evidence;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(4)(d)(ii): the warrant requirement;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(4)(d)(iii): exceptions to the warrant requirement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(4)(d)(iv): removing a child from the custody of the child's parent or guardian.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(5): 80-1-102 The division shall train the division's child welfare caseworkers to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(5)(a): 80-1-102 apply the risk assessment tools and rules described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(5)(b): develop child and family plans that comply with:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(5)(b)(i): federal mandates; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(5)(b)(ii): the specific needs of the child and the child's family.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(6): The division shall use the training of child welfare caseworkers to emphasize:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(6)(a): the importance of maintaining the parent-child relationship;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(6)(b): the preference for providing in-home services over taking a child into protective custody, both for the emotional well-being of the child and the efficient allocation of resources; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(6)(c): the importance and priority of:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(6)(c)(i): kinship placement in the event a child must be taken into protective custody; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(6)(c)(ii): guardianship placement, in the event the parent-child relationship is legally terminated and no appropriate adoptive placement is available.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(7): If a child welfare caseworker is hired, before assuming independent casework responsibilities, the division shall ensure that the child welfare caseworker has:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(7)(a): completed the training described in Subsections (4), (5), and (6); and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-402(7)(b): participated in sufficient skills development for a child welfare caseworker.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-403 Child welfare caseworker safety and risk assessments.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-403(1): A child welfare caseworker within the division shall use evidence-informed or evidence-based safety and risk assessments to guide decisions concerning a child throughout a child protection investigation or proceeding.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-403(2): As part of an evidence-informed or evidence-based safety and risk assessment, the child welfare caseworker shall assess at least the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-403(2)(a): threat to the child's safety;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-403(2)(b): protective capabilities of a parent or guardian, including the parent or guardian's readiness, willingness, and ability to plan for the child's safety;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-403(2)(c): the child's particular vulnerabilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-403(2)(d): interventions required to protect the child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-403(2)(e): likelihood of future harm to the child.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405 Private recruitment and training of foster care parents and child welfare volunteers -- Extension of immunity.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(1)(a): "Referring entity" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(1)(a)(i): an incorporated or unincorporated organization or association whether formally incorporated or otherwise established and operating for religious, charitable, or educational purposes, that does not distribute any of the organization's or association's income or assets to the organization's or association's members, directors, officers, or other participants;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(1)(a)(ii): an organization described in Section 501(c)(3) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986 and is exempt from tax under Section 501 of the Internal Revenue Code; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(1)(a)(iii): any not-for-profit organization which is formed and conducted for public benefit and operated primarily for charitable, civic, educational, religious, benevolent, welfare, or health purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(1)(b): "Referring individual" means an individual:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(1)(b)(i): with the authority to act on behalf of a referring entity in making a referral; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(1)(b)(ii): who may or may not be compensated by the referring entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(2): The division may contract with one or more private, nonprofit organizations to recruit and train foster care parents and child welfare volunteers on a statewide or regional basis.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3): (2); (3); (3) An organization that contracts with the division under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(a): increase the number of licensed and trained foster care parents in the geographic area covered by:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(a)(i): developing a strategic plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(a)(ii): assessing the needs, perceptions, and qualities of potential foster care parents;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(a)(iii): assessing the needs, perceptions, and qualities of children in state custody;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(a)(iv): identifying potential foster care parents through public and private resources;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(a)(v): screening foster care parent applicants;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(a)(vi): providing preservice, ongoing, and customized training to foster care parents;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(a)(vii): developing a competency-based training curriculum with input from public and private resources and approved by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(a)(viii): focusing training exercises on skill development; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(a)(ix): supporting foster care parents by supplying staff support, identifying common issues, encouraging peer support, and connecting available resources;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(b): increase the number of child welfare volunteers in the geographical area covered by:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(b)(i): developing a strategic plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(b)(ii): seeking the participation of established volunteer organizations;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(b)(iii): designing and offering initial orientation sessions to child welfare volunteers;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(b)(iv): informing volunteers of options for service as specified by the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(b)(v): facilitating the placement and certification of child welfare volunteers;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(c): coordinate efforts, if appropriate, with the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(d): (3) seek private contributions in furtherance of the organization's activities under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(e): perform other related services and activities as may be required by the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(3)(f): (3) establish a system for evaluating performance and obtaining feedback on the activities performed under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(4): (3) Notwithstanding Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(4)(a): initial and ongoing training content, material, curriculum, and techniques, and certification standards used by an organization; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(4)(b): screening, investigation, licensing, certification, referral, and placement decisions with respect to any individual recruited or trained by an organization.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(5): (4); (5)(a); 80-2-602
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(5)(a): (4) An organization under contract with the department and the department's directors, trustees, officers, employees, and agents, whether compensated or not, may not be held civilly liable for any act or omission on a matter for which the department retains ultimate authority and responsibility under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(5)(b): (5)(a); 80-2-602 Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(6): A referring entity or a referring individual that voluntarily and without remuneration assists an organization to identify and recruit foster care parents or child welfare volunteers is not liable in any civil action for any act or omission of:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(6)(a): the referring entity or referring individual that is performed in good faith and in furtherance of the entity's assistance to the organization; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-405(6)(b): any individual directly or indirectly referred to the organization by the entity as a foster care parent or child welfare volunteer, if the referring individual was without actual knowledge of any substantiated fact that would have disqualified the individual who was referred from such a position at the time the referral was made.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503 Division contracts for prevention and treatment of child abuse and neglect -- Requirements -- Public hearing -- Funding provided by contractor.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(1)(a): The Legislature finds that there is a need to assist private and public agencies in identifying and establishing community-based education, service, and treatment programs to prevent the occurrence and recurrence of abuse and neglect.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(1)(b): It is the purpose of this section to provide a means to increase prevention and treatment programs designed to reduce the occurrence or recurrence of child abuse and neglect.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(2): The division shall contract with public or private nonprofit organizations, agencies, or schools, or with qualified individuals to establish voluntary community-based educational and service programs designed to reduce or prevent the occurrence or recurrence of abuse and neglect.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(3): (3)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(3)(a): A program that the division contracts with under this section shall provide voluntary primary abuse and neglect prevention, and voluntary or court-ordered treatment services.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(3)(b): (3)(a) A program described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(3)(b)(i): a program related to prenatal care, perinatal bonding, child growth and development, basic child care, care of children with special needs, and coping with family stress;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(3)(b)(ii): a program related to crisis care, aid to parents, abuse counseling, support groups for abusive or potentially abusive parents and abusive parents' children, and early identification of families where the potential for abuse and neglect exists;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(3)(b)(iii): a program clearly designed to prevent the occurrence or recurrence of abuse, neglect, sexual abuse, sexual exploitation, or medical or educational neglect;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(3)(b)(iv): a program that the division and council consider potentially effective in reducing the incidence of family problems leading to abuse or neglect; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(3)(b)(v): a program designed to establish and assist community resources that prevent abuse and neglect.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(4): (6); Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(4)(a): consult with appropriate state agencies, commissions, and boards to help determine the probable effectiveness, fiscal soundness, and need for proposed education and service programs for the prevention and treatment of abuse and neglect;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(4)(b): develop policies to determine whether a program will be discontinued or receive continuous funding;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(4)(c): facilitate the exchange of information between and among groups concerned with families and children;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(4)(d): establish flexible fees and fee schedules based on the recipient's ability to pay for part or all of the costs of service received;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(4)(e): (6) before awarding a contract for an abuse or neglect prevention or treatment program or service:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(4)(e)(i): (6) conduct a public hearing to receive public comment on the program or service and ensure the council conducted a public hearing on the program or service in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(4)(e)(ii): if the program or service is intended for presentation in public schools, receive evidence that the program or service is approved by the local board of education of each school district that will be utilizing the program or service, or under the direction of the local board of education, the state superintendent; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(4)(e)(iii): consider need, diversity of geographic locations, the program's or services' coordination with or enhancement of existing services, and the program's or services' extensive use of volunteers;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(4)(f): award a contract under this section for services to prevent abuse and neglect on the basis of probability of success, based in part on sound research data; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(4)(g): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act adopt rules in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(5): (5)(a) The division may:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(5)(a): require that 25% of the funding for a program contracted for under this section be provided by the contractor operating the program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(5)(b): (5)(a) consider a contribution of materials, supplies, or physical facilities as all or part of the funding provided by the contractor under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(6): The council shall conduct a public hearing to receive public comment on the program or service before the division may enter into a contract under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503(7): A contract entered into under this section shall contain a provision for the evaluation of services provided under the contract.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5 Psychotropic medication oversight program -- Behavioral health service rates.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(1): 26B-1-204; 80-6-703 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(1)(a): "Advanced practice registered nurse" means an individual licensed to practice as an advanced practice registered nurse in this state under Title 58, Chapter 31b, Nurse Practice Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(1)(b): 26B-1-204 "Division" means the Division of Integrated Healthcare created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(1)(c): "HIPAA" means 45 C.F.R. Parts 160, 162, and 164, Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act of 1996, as amended.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(1)(d): "Physician assistant" means an individual licensed to practice as a physician assistant in this state under Title 58, Chapter 70a, Utah Physician Assistant Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(1)(e): "Psychotropic medication" means medication prescribed to affect or alter thought processes, mood, or behavior, including antipsychotic, antidepressant, anxiolytic, or behavior medication.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(1)(f): 80-6-703 "Qualifying minor" means a minor committed to the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(2): The division shall, through contract with the University of Utah or another qualified third party, operate a psychotropic medication oversight program for children in foster care and qualifying minors to ensure that each foster child and qualifying minor is prescribed psychotropic medication consistent with the foster child's or qualifying minor's needs and consistent with clinical best practices.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(3): The division shall operate an oversight team to manage the psychotropic medication oversight program, composed of at least the following individuals:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(3)(a): a physician assistant with pediatric mental health experience, or an advanced practice registered nurse with pediatric mental health experience, contracted with the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(3)(b): a child psychiatrist contracted with the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(3)(c): a data analyst contracted with the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(3)(d): an individual with care coordination experience.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(4): The oversight team shall monitor foster children and qualifying minors:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(4)(a): six years old or younger who are being prescribed one or more psychotropic medications;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(4)(b): seven years old or older who are being prescribed two or more psychotropic medications; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(4)(c): who are prescribed one or more antipsychotic medications.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(5): The division shall establish a business associate agreement with the oversight team by which the oversight team shall, upon request, be given information or records related to the foster child's or qualifying minor's health care history, including psychotropic medication history and mental and behavioral health history, from:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(5)(a): the division's Medicaid pharmacy program;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(5)(b): the department's written and electronic records and databases;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(5)(c): the foster child's current or past caseworker, or the qualifying minor's current or past case manager;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(5)(d): the foster child or qualifying minor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(5)(e): the foster child's or qualifying minor's:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(5)(e)(i): current or past health care provider;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(5)(e)(ii): natural parents; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(5)(e)(iii): foster parents.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(6): The oversight team may review and monitor the following information about a foster child or qualifying minor:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(6)(a): the foster child's or qualifying minor's history;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(6)(b): the foster child's or qualifying minor's health care, including psychotropic medication history and mental or behavioral health history;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(6)(c): whether there are less invasive treatment options available to meet the foster child's or qualifying minor's needs;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(6)(d): the dosage or dosage range and appropriateness of the foster child's or qualifying minor's psychotropic medication;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(6)(e): the short-term or long-term risks associated with the use of the foster child's or qualifying minor's psychotropic medication; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(6)(f): the reported benefits of the foster child's or qualifying minor's psychotropic medication.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(7): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(7)(a): On at least a quarterly basis, the oversight team shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(7)(a)(i): review the medical and mental or behavioral health history for each foster child and qualifying minor overseen by the program;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(7)(a)(ii): based on the review under Subsection (7)(a)(i), document the oversight team's findings and recommendations; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(7)(a)(iii): make written recommendations concerning the foster child's or qualifying minor's psychotropic medication and the foster child's or qualifying minor's mental or behavioral health, including any recommendation for psychotherapy treatment.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(7)(b): The oversight team's recommendations described in Subsection (7)(a) shall be provided to the foster child's current caseworker or the qualifying minor's current case manager, the foster child's or qualifying minor's parent or guardian, and the foster child's or qualifying minor's current health care providers, in accordance with rules adopted pursuant to Subsection (8) and in compliance with HIPAA and other relevant state and federal privacy laws.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(7)(c): The member of the oversight team described in Subsection (3)(d) shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(7)(c)(i): provide the recommendations described in Subsection (7)(a) in writing and verbally, or as otherwise provided in rules adopted pursuant to Subsection (8), to the foster child's or qualifying minor's current health care providers; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(7)(c)(ii): on at least a semiannual basis, follow up with the foster child's or qualifying minor's current health care providers to document whether recommendations made by the oversight team have been implemented.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(7)(d): A foster child's caseworker or qualifying minor's case manager shall maintain a confidential record of recommendations provided under Subsection (7)(b).
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(8): The division may adopt administrative rules in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, necessary to administer this section, including the rules described in Subsection (7)(b).
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(9): The division shall report regarding the psychotropic medication oversight program:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(9)(a): to the Child Welfare Legislative Oversight Panel by October 1 of each even numbered year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(9)(b): orally to the Health and Human Services Interim Committee, at least once every two years at or before the October interim meeting.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(10): The oversight team shall report:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(10)(a): quarterly to the division regarding the number of foster children and qualifying minors reviewed and the number of recommendations made; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(10)(b): annually to the division regarding outcomes for foster children and qualifying minors overseen by the program.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-503.5(11): Beginning on July 1, 2024, the department shall pay for outpatient behavioral health services for children in foster care and qualifying minors at a rate no lower than the standard Medicaid fee schedule.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-601 Legislative purpose.
---------------------------------------------------
It is the purpose of this part to protect the best interests of children, offer protective services to prevent harm to children, stabilize the home environment, preserve family life whenever possible, and encourage cooperation among the states in dealing with the problem of abuse or neglect.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602 Child abuse and neglect reporting requirements -- Exceptions.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(1): Except as provided in Subsection (3), if a person, including an individual licensed under Title 58, Chapter 31b, Nurse Practice Act, or Title 58, Chapter 67, Utah Medical Practice Act, has reason to believe that a child is, or has been, the subject of abuse or neglect, or observes a child being subjected to conditions or circumstances that would reasonably result in abuse or neglect, the person shall immediately report the suspected abuse or neglect to the division or to the nearest peace officer or law enforcement agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(2): 80-2-701
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(2)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(2)(a)(i): If a peace officer or law enforcement agency receives a report under Subsection (1), the peace officer or law enforcement agency shall immediately notify the nearest office of the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(2)(a)(ii): If the division receives a report under Subsection (1), the division shall immediately notify the appropriate local law enforcement agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(2)(b): 80-2-701
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(2)(b)(i): 80-2-701 The division shall, in addition to the division's own investigation in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(2)(b)(ii): If a law enforcement agency undertakes an investigation of a report under Subsection (1), the law enforcement agency shall provide a final investigatory report to the division upon request.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(3): Subject to Subsection (4), the reporting requirement described in Subsection (1) does not apply to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(3)(a): a member of the clergy, with regard to any confession made to the member of the clergy while functioning in the ministerial capacity of the member of the clergy and without the consent of the individual making the confession, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(3)(a)(i): the perpetrator made the confession directly to the member of the clergy; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(3)(a)(ii): the member of the clergy is, under canon law or church doctrine or practice, bound to maintain the confidentiality of the confession; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(3)(b): an attorney, or an individual employed by the attorney, if the knowledge or belief of the suspected abuse or neglect of a child arises from the representation of a client, unless the attorney is permitted to reveal the suspected abuse or neglect of the child to prevent reasonably certain death or substantial bodily harm in accordance with Utah Rules of Professional Conduct, Rule 1.6.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(4)(a): When a member of the clergy receives information about abuse or neglect from any source other than confession of the perpetrator, the member of the clergy is required to report the information even if the member of the clergy also received information about the abuse or neglect from the confession of the perpetrator.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(4)(b): When a member of the clergy reasonably believes that a child is the subject of ongoing abuse or neglect, the member of the clergy may report the information even if the perpetrator made a confession to the member of the clergy regarding the abuse or neglect.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(4)(c): Exemption of the reporting requirement for an individual described in Subsection (3) does not exempt the individual from any other efforts required by law to prevent further abuse or neglect by the perpetrator.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(4)(d): A report by a member of the clergy under Subsection (4) is not intended to have any effect on the application of a privilege outlined in the Utah Rules of Evidence.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(5): The physician-patient privilege does not:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(5)(a): excuse an individual who is licensed under Title 58, Chapter 67, Utah Medical Practice Act, or Title 58, Chapter 68, Utah Osteopathic Medical Practice Act, from reporting under this section; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-602(5)(b): constitute grounds for excluding evidence regarding the child's injuries, or the cause of the child's injuries, in a judicial or administrative proceeding resulting from a report under this section.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-603(1)(d)(ii)(B): Title 26B, Chapter 4, Part 2, Cannabinoid Research and Medical Cannabis obtained in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-603(2): A health care provider who attends the birth of a newborn child or cares for a newborn child and determines the following, shall report the determination to the division as soon as possible:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-603(2)(a): the newborn child:

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(1)(b): 80-3-409
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(1)(b)(i): who has permanency goals of adoption; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(1)(b)(ii): 80-3-409 for whom a final plan for pursuing termination of parental rights is approved in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(2): 80-2-809
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(2)(a): 80-2-809 "Adoption assistance" means, except as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(2)(b): "Adoption assistance" includes state medical assistance, reimbursement of nonrecurring adoption expenses, or monthly subsidies.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(3): 80-2-806; 80-2-301 "Adoption services" means, except as used in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(3)(a): placing children for adoption;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(3)(b): 80-2-301 subsidizing adoptions under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(3)(c): supervising adoption placements until the adoption is finalized by a court;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(3)(d): conducting adoption studies;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(3)(e): preparing adoption reports upon request of the court; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(3)(f): providing postadoptive placement services, upon request of a family, for the purpose of stabilizing a possible disruptive placement.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(4): "Child who has a special need" means a child who:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(4)(a): cannot or should not be returned to the home of the child's biological parents; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(4)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(4)(b)(i): is five years old or older;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(4)(b)(ii): is under 18 years old with a physical, emotional, or mental disability; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(4)(b)(iii): is a member of a sibling group placed together for adoption.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(5): "Monthly subsidy" means financial support to assist with the costs of adopting and caring for a child who has a special need.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(6): "Nonrecurring adoption expenses" means reasonably necessary adoption fees, court costs, attorney's fees, and other expenses which are directly related to the legal adoption of a child who has a special need.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(7): 26-18-2 "State medical assistance" means the Medicaid program and medical assistance as those terms are defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(8): "Supplemental adoption assistance" means financial support for extraordinary, infrequent, or uncommon documented needs not otherwise covered by a monthly subsidy, state medical assistance, or other public benefits for which a child who has a special need is eligible.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-801(9): "Vendor services" means services that a person provides under contract with the division.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-805(2)(a): The division shall, to the extent that sufficient funds are available, use out-of-home services funds or division-designated post-adopt funds to provide services to a child who is adopted from the custody of the division, without requiring that the child's parent terminate parental rights, or that the child's parent or legal guardian transfer or surrender custodial rights, in order to receive the services.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-806 Division adoption assistance -- Eligibility -- Limitations.
