Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-808 Division termination or modification of adoption assistance.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-808(1): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act The division may not terminate or modify adoption assistance unless the division gives the adoptive parents notice and opportunity for a hearing as required in
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-808(2): (3) The division shall terminate adoption assistance if any of the following occur:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-808(2)(a): the adoptive parents request termination;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-808(2)(b): (3) subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-808(2)(c): the child dies;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-808(2)(d): the adoptive parents die;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-808(2)(e): the adoptive parents' legal responsibility for the child ceases;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-808(2)(f): the state determines that the child is no longer receiving support from the adoptive parents;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-808(2)(g): the child marries; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-808(2)(h): the child enters military service.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-808(3): Adoption assistance may not continue after the day on which the child reaches 21 years old.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809 Interstate compact adoption assistance agreements.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(1): 80-2-801 Notwithstanding Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(1)(a): "Adoption assistance" means financial support to an adoptive parent provided under the Adoption Assistance and Child Welfare Act of 1980, Title IV (e) of the Social Security Act, and Title XIX of the Social Security Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(1)(b): "Adoption assistance agreement" means a written agreement between the division and adoptive parents, or between any other state and adoptive parents, providing for adoption assistance.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(2): The division may develop and negotiate an interstate compact for the provision of medical identification and assistance to an adoptive parent who receives adoption assistance.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(3): (2) An interstate compact under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(3)(a): a provision:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(3)(a)(i): for joinder by all states;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(3)(a)(ii): for withdrawal from the compact upon written notice to the parties, with a period of one year between the date of the notice and the effective date of withdrawal;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(3)(a)(iii): that a child who is the subject of an adoption assistance agreement with another party state, and who subsequently becomes a resident of this state, shall receive medical identification and assistance in this state under the Adoption Assistance and Child Welfare Act of 1980, Title IV (e) of the Social Security Act, and Title XIX of the Social Security Act, based on the child's adoption assistance agreement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(3)(a)(iv): that a child who is the subject of an adoption assistance agreement with the division, and who subsequently becomes a resident of another party state, shall receive medical identification and assistance from that state under the Adoption and Child Welfare Act of 1980, Title IV (e) of the Social Security Act, and Title XIX of the Social Security Act, based on his adoption assistance agreement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(3)(b): a requirement that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(3)(b)(i): each instance of adoption assistance to which the compact applies be covered by an adoption assistance agreement between the adoptive parents and the agency of the state that initially agrees to provide adoption assistance;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(3)(b)(ii): any agreement is expressly for the benefit of the adopted child and is enforceable by the adoptive parent, and by the state agency providing adoption assistance; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(3)(b)(iii): the protections of the interstate compact continue for the duration of the adoption assistance and apply to all children and the children's adoptive parents who receive adoption assistance from a party state other than the state in which the children reside.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(4)(a): The division:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(4)(a)(i): shall provide services to a child who is the subject of an adoption assistance agreement executed by the division, and who is a resident of another state, if the services are not provided by the child's residence state under an interstate compact; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(4)(a)(ii): may reimburse the adoptive parent upon receipt of evidence of the adoptive parent's payment for services for which the child is eligible, which were not paid by the residence state, and are not covered by insurance or other third party medical contract.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-809(4)(b): The services provided under this subsection are the services for which there is no federal contribution, or which, if federally aided, are not provided by the residence state.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-901 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-901(1): "State" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-901(1)(a): a state of the United States;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-901(1)(b): the District of Columbia;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-901(1)(c): the Commonwealth of Puerto Rico;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-901(1)(d): the Virgin Islands;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-901(1)(e): Guam;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-901(1)(f): the Commonwealth of the Northern Mariana Islands; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-901(1)(g): a territory or possession administered by the United States.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-901(2): "State plan" means the written description of the programs for children, youth, and family services administered by the division in accordance with federal law.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-902 Division authority under Article III of Interstate Compact.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-902(1): The "appropriate public authorities," as used in Article III of the Interstate Compact on the Placement of Children shall, with reference to this state, mean the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-902(2): The division shall receive and act with reference to notices required by Article III of the compact.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-903 Director authority under Article V of Interstate Compact.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
As used in Paragraph (1) of Article V of the Interstate Compact on the Placement of Children, "appropriate authority in the receiving state," with reference to this state, means the director of the division.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-904 Executive director authority under Article VII of Interstate Compact.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-904(1): As used in Article VII of the Interstate Compact on the Placement of Children, "executive" means the executive director of the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-904(2): The executive director of the department is authorized to appoint a compact administrator in accordance with the terms of Article VII of the compact.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-905 Interstate Compact on Placement of Children -- Text.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The Interstate Compact on the Placement of Children is hereby enacted and entered into with all other jurisdictions that legally join in the compact which is, in form, substantially as follows:  INTERSTATE COMPACT ON PLACEMENT OF CHILDREN  ARTICLE I  Purpose and Policy

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-906 Financial responsibility for child placed under Interstate Compact.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-906(1): Financial responsibility for a child placed under the provisions of the Interstate Compact on the Placement of Children shall, in the first instance, be determined in accordance with the provisions of Article V of the compact.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-906(2): In the event of partial or complete default of performance under the compact, the provisions of Title 81, Chapter 6, Child Support, may also be invoked.

Requirements for visitation, inspection, or supervision of children, homes, institutions, or other agencies in another party state which may apply under this chapter or

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-908 Jurisdiction over delinquent children under Interstate Compact.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Any court having jurisdiction to place delinquent children may place such a child in an institution in another state, under Article VI of the Interstate Compact on the Placement of Children, and shall retain jurisdiction as provided in Article V of the compact.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1006 Sharing of records with Indian tribe under agreement.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If the division has a privacy agreement with an Indian tribe to protect the confidentiality of division records regarding an Indian child to the same extent that the division is required to protect other division records, the division shall cooperate with and share all appropriate information in the division's possession regarding an Indian child, the Indian child's parent or guardian, or a proposed placement for the Indian child with the Indian tribe that is affiliated with the Indian child.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102 Performance monitoring system -- Report.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(1)(a): "Performance indicators" means actual performance in a program, activity, or other function for which there is a performance standard.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(1)(b): "Performance standards" means the targeted or expected level of performance of each area in the child welfare system, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(1)(b)(i): child protection services;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(1)(b)(ii): adoption;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(1)(b)(iii): in-home services;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(1)(b)(iv): foster care;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(1)(b)(v): other substitute care.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(1)(b)(vi): qualitative case review; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(1)(b)(vii): case review process.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2): (2)(c); (2)(c); (2)(e); (2)(c); (4)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(a): The division shall create performance standards.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(b): The division may not amend performance standards unless the amendment is:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(b)(i): necessary and proper for the effective administration of the division; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(b)(ii): necessary to comply with, or implement changes in, the law.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(c): Before amending the performance standards, the division shall provide written notice of the proposed amendment to the council.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(d): (2)(c) The notice described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(d)(i): the proposed amendment;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(d)(ii): a summary of the reason for the proposed amendment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(d)(iii): the proposed effective date of the amendment.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(e): (2)(c) Within 45 days after the day on which the division provides the notice described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(f): (2)(e); (2)(c) The division may not implement a proposed amendment to the performance standards until the earlier of:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(f)(i): (2)(e) seven days after the day on which the division receives the written comments regarding the proposed change described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(f)(ii): (2)(c) 52 days after the day on which the division provides the notice described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(g): (4) The division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(g)(i): give full, fair, and good faith consideration to all comments and objections received from the council;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(g)(ii): notify the council in writing of:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(g)(ii)(A): the division's decision regarding the proposed amendment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(g)(ii)(B): the reasons that support the decision;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(g)(iii): (4) include complete information on all amendments to the performance standards in the report described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(2)(g)(iv): post the changes on the division's website.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(3): The division shall maintain a performance monitoring system to regularly:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(3)(a): collect information on performance indicators; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(3)(b): compare performance indicators to performance standards.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(4): Before January 1 of each year, the director shall submit a written report to the Child Welfare Legislative Oversight Panel and the Social Services Appropriations Subcommittee that includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(4)(a): a comparison between the performance indicators for the prior fiscal year and the performance standards;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(4)(b): for each performance indicator that does not meet the performance standard:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(4)(b)(i): the reason the standard was not met;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(4)(b)(ii): the measures that need to be taken to meet the standard; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(4)(b)(iii): the division's plan to comply with the standard for the current fiscal year;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(4)(c): data on the extent to which new and experienced division employees have received training under statute, administrative rule, and division policy; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1102(4)(d): an analysis of the use and efficacy of in-home services, both before and after removal of a child from the child's home.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104 Child protection ombudsman -- Responsibility -- Authority -- Report.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(1)(a): "Complainant" means a person who initiates a complaint with the ombudsman.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(1)(b): "Complaint" means a complaint regarding an act or omission by the division with respect to a particular child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(1)(c): "Ombudsman" means the child protection ombudsman appointed under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(2)(a): There is created within the department the position of child protection ombudsman.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(2)(b): The executive director of the department shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(2)(b)(i): appoint an ombudsman who has:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(2)(b)(i)(A): recognized executive and administrative capacity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(2)(b)(i)(B): experience in child welfare, and in state laws and policies governing abused, neglected, and dependent children; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(2)(b)(ii): select the ombudsman solely with regard to qualifications and fitness to discharge the duties of the ombudsman.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(2)(c): The ombudsman shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(2)(c)(i): serve at the pleasure of the executive director of the department; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(2)(c)(ii): devote full-time to the duties described in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3): The ombudsman shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(a): unless the ombudsman decides not to investigate the complaint, upon receipt of a complaint, investigate whether an act or omission of the division with respect to a particular child:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(a)(i): is contrary to statute, rule, or policy;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(a)(ii): places a child's health or safety at risk;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(a)(iii): is made without an adequate statement of reason; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(a)(iv): is based on irrelevant, immaterial, or erroneous grounds;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(b): notify the complainant and the division of:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(b)(i): the ombudsman's decision to investigate or not investigate the complaint; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(b)(ii): if the ombudsman decides not to investigate the complaint, the reason for the decision;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(c): if the ombudsman finds that a person's act or omission violates state or federal criminal law, immediately report the finding to the appropriate county or district attorney or to the attorney general;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(d): immediately notify the division if the ombudsman finds that a child needs protective custody;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(e): prepare a written report of the findings and recommendations, if any, of each investigation;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(f): make recommendations to the division if the ombudsman finds that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(f)(i): a matter should be further considered by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(f)(ii): an administrative act should be addressed, modified, or canceled;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(f)(iii): action should be taken by the division with regard to one of the division's employees; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(f)(iv): any other action should be taken by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(g): subject to Subsection (3), in accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, make rules that govern the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(g)(i): receiving and processing a complaint;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(g)(ii): notifying a complainant and the division regarding a decision to investigate or to decline to investigate a complaint;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(g)(iii): prioritizing workload;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(g)(iv): maximum time within which an investigation is required to be completed;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(g)(v): conducting an investigation;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(g)(vi): notifying a complainant and the division regarding the results of an investigation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(g)(vii): making recommendations based on the findings and results of investigations;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(h): within appropriations from the Legislature, employ staff as may be necessary to carry out the ombudsman's duties under this section;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(i): provide information regarding the role, duties, and functions of the ombudsman to public agencies, private entities, and individuals; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(3)(j): as appropriate, make recommendations to the division regarding individual child welfare cases, and the rules, policies, and operations of the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(4)(a): The ombudsman may:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(4)(a)(i): decline to investigate a complaint or continue an investigation of a complaint;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(4)(a)(ii): conduct an investigation on the ombudsman's own initiative;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(4)(a)(iii): conduct further investigation upon the request of the complainant or upon the ombudsman's own initiative; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(4)(a)(iv): advise a complainant to pursue administrative remedies or channels of a complaint before pursuing a complaint with the ombudsman.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(4)(b): Subsection (4)(a)(iv) does not prevent a complainant from making a complaint directly to the ombudsman before pursuing an administrative remedy.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(5)(a): A record of the ombudsman regarding an individual child welfare case shall be classified in accordance with federal law and Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(5)(b): The ombudsman shall have access to all of the department's written and electronic records and databases, including those regarding individual child welfare cases.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2-1104(5)(c): In accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 2, Government Records Access and Management Act, all documents and information received by the ombudsman shall maintain the same classification that was designated by the department.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-101 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-101(1): 80-2-102 "Custody" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-101(2): 80-2-201 "Division" means the Division of Child and Family Services created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-101(3): "Friend" means an adult who:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-101(3)(a): has an established relationship with the child or a family member of the child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-101(3)(b): is not the natural parent of the child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-101(4): "Nonrelative" means an individual who is not a noncustodial parent or relative.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-101(5): "Relative" means an adult who:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-101(5)(a): is the child's grandparent, great grandparent, aunt, great aunt, uncle, great uncle, brother-in-law, sister-in-law, stepparent, first cousin, stepsibling, or sibling;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-101(5)(b): is the first cousin of the child's parent;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-101(5)(c): is a permanent guardian or natural parent of the child's sibling; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-101(5)(d): in the case of a child who is an Indian child, is an extended family member as defined in the Indian Child Welfare Act, 25 U.S.C. Sec. 1903.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-101(6): 80-2-102 "Sibling" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-101(7): 80-2-102 "Temporary custody" means the same as that term is defined in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201 Rights of parents -- Children's rights -- Interest and responsibility of state.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(1): (2); (7); (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(1)(a): Under both the United States Constitution and the constitution of this state, a parent possesses a fundamental liberty interest in the care, custody, and management of the parent's children. A fundamentally fair process must be provided to parents if the state moves to challenge or interfere with parental rights. A governmental entity must support any actions or allegations made in opposition to the rights and desires of a parent regarding the parent's child by sufficient evidence to satisfy a parent's constitutional entitlement to heightened protection against government interference with the parent's fundamental rights and liberty interests and, concomitantly, the right of the child to be reared by the child's natural parent.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(1)(b): The fundamental liberty interest of a parent concerning the care, custody, and management of the parent's child is recognized, protected, and does not cease to exist simply because a parent may fail to be a model parent or because the parent's child is placed in the temporary custody of the state. At all times, a parent retains a vital interest in preventing the irretrievable destruction of family life. Before an adjudication of unfitness, government action in relation to a parent and the parent's child may not exceed the least restrictive means or alternatives available to accomplish a compelling state interest. Until the state proves parental unfitness, and the child suffers, or is substantially likely to suffer, serious detriment as a result, the child and the child's parent share a vital interest in preventing erroneous termination of their natural relationship and the state cannot presume that a child and the child's parent are adversaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(1)(c): It is in the best interest and welfare of a child to be raised under the care and supervision of the child's natural parents. A child's need for a normal family life in a permanent home, and for positive, nurturing family relationships is usually best met by the child's natural parents. Additionally, the integrity of the family unit and the right of a parent to conceive and raise the parent's child are constitutionally protected. The right of a fit, competent parent to raise the parent's child without undue government interference is a fundamental liberty interest that has long been protected by the laws and Constitution and is a fundamental public policy of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(1)(d): The state recognizes that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(1)(d)(i): a parent has the right, obligation, responsibility, and authority to raise, manage, train, educate, provide and care for, and reasonably discipline the parent's child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(1)(d)(ii): the state's role is secondary and supportive to the primary role of a parent.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(1)(e): It is the public policy of this state that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(1)(e)(i): a parent retains the fundamental right and duty to exercise primary control over the care, supervision, upbringing, and education of the parent's child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(1)(e)(ii): a parent retains the right to have contact with the parent's child when the child is placed outside of the parent's home, and parent-time should be ordered by a court so long as the contact is not contrary to the best interest of the child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(1)(e)(iii): a child has the right to have contact with the child's sibling when the child is placed outside of the home and apart from the child's sibling, and sibling visits should be ordered by a court unless the contact would be contrary to the safety or well-being of the child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(1)(f): (2); (7); (1) Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(2): It is also the public policy of this state that children have the right to protection from abuse and neglect, and that the state retains a compelling interest in investigating, prosecuting, and punishing abuse and neglect. Therefore, the state, as parens patriae, has an interest in and responsibility to protect a child whose parent abuses the child or does not adequately provide for the child's welfare. There may be circumstances where a parent's conduct or condition is a substantial departure from the norm and the parent is unable or unwilling to render safe and proper parental care and protection. Under those circumstances, the state may take action for the welfare and protection of the parent's child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(3): When the division intervenes on behalf of an abused, neglected, or dependent child, the division shall take into account the child's need for protection from immediate harm and the extent to which the child's extended family may provide needed protection. Throughout the division's involvement, the division shall utilize the least intrusive and least restrictive means available to protect a child, in an effort to ensure that children are brought up in stable, permanent families, rather than in temporary foster placements under the supervision of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(4): Chapter 3, Abuse, Neglect, and Dependency Proceedings If circumstances within the family pose a threat to the child's immediate safety or welfare, the division may seek custody of the child for a planned, temporary period and place the child in a safe environment, subject to the requirements of this section and in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(5): 80-2a-302 In determining and making reasonable efforts with regard to a child, under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(6): 80-2a-302(4); 80-3-301(12); (6) In accordance with Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(7): (1); (5); (6); Chapter 4, Termination and Restoration of Parental Rights
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(7)(a): (1) In accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(7)(b): (5); (6) If the use or continuation of reasonable efforts, as described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(7)(c): Chapter 4, Termination and Restoration of Parental Rights Subject to the parental rights recognized and protected under this section, if, because of a parent's conduct or condition, the parent is determined to be unfit or incompetent based on the grounds for termination of parental rights described in
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-201(8): 80-1-102(58)(b)(i); (iii); 80-3-109; 80-3-304 The state's right to direct or intervene in the provision of medical or mental health care for a child is subject to Subsections


Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202 Removal of a child by a peace officer or child welfare caseworker -- Search warrants -- Protective custody and temporary care of a child.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(1): A peace officer or child welfare caseworker may remove a child or take a child into protective custody, temporary custody, or custody in accordance with this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(2): 26B-4-201
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(2)(a): Except as provided in Subsection (2)(b), a peace officer or a child welfare caseworker may not enter the home of a child whose case is not under the jurisdiction of the juvenile court, remove a child from the child's home or school, or take a child into protective custody unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(2)(a)(i): there exist exigent circumstances sufficient to relieve the peace officer or the child welfare caseworker of the requirement to obtain a search warrant under Subsection (3);
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(2)(a)(ii): the peace officer or child welfare caseworker obtains a search warrant under Subsection (3);
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(2)(a)(iii): the peace officer or child welfare caseworker obtains a court order after the child's parent or guardian is given notice and an opportunity to be heard; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(2)(a)(iv): the peace officer or child welfare caseworker obtains the consent of the child's parent or guardian.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(2)(b): 26B-4-201 A peace officer or a child welfare caseworker may not take action under Subsection (2)(a) solely on the basis of:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(2)(b)(i): educational neglect, truancy, or failure to comply with a court order to attend school;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(2)(b)(ii): 26B-4-201 the possession or use, in accordance with Title 26B, Chapter 4, Part 2, Cannabinoid Research and Medical Cannabis, of cannabis in a medicinal dosage form, a cannabis product in a medicinal dosage form, or a medical cannabis device, as those terms are defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(2)(b)(iii): a parent's agreement or disagreement with a minor child of the couple's:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(2)(b)(iii)(A): assertion that the child's gender identity is different from the child's biological sex; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(2)(b)(iii)(B): practice of having or expressing a different gender identity than the child's biological sex.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(3): 77-23-210
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(3)(a): The juvenile court may issue a warrant authorizing a peace officer or a child welfare caseworker to search for a child and take the child into protective custody if it appears to the juvenile court upon a verified petition, recorded sworn testimony or an affidavit sworn to by a peace officer or another individual, and upon the examination of other witnesses if required by the juvenile court, that there is probable cause to believe that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(3)(a)(i): there is a threat of substantial harm to the child's health or safety;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(3)(a)(ii): it is necessary to take the child into protective custody to avoid the harm described in Subsection (3)(a)(i); and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(3)(a)(iii): it is likely that the child will suffer substantial harm if the child's parent or guardian is given notice and an opportunity to be heard before the child is taken into protective custody.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(3)(b): 77-23-210 In accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(4)(a): A child welfare caseworker may take action under Subsection (2) accompanied by a peace officer or without a peace officer if a peace officer is not reasonably available.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(4)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(4)(b)(i): Before taking a child into protective custody, and if possible and consistent with the child's safety and welfare, a child welfare caseworker shall determine whether there are services available that, if provided to a parent or guardian of the child, would eliminate the need to remove the child from the custody of the child's parent or guardian.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(4)(b)(ii): In determining whether the services described in Subsection (4)(b)(i) are reasonably available, the child welfare caseworker shall consider the child's health, safety, and welfare as the paramount concern.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(4)(b)(iii): If the child welfare caseworker determines the services described in Subsection (4)(b)(i) are reasonably available, the services shall be utilized.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(5): 80-2a-203; 80-2a-301
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(5)(a): 80-2a-203 If a peace officer or a child welfare caseworker takes a child into protective custody under Subsection (2), the peace officer or child welfare caseworker shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(5)(a)(i): 80-2a-203 notify the child's parent or guardian in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(5)(a)(ii): release the child to the care of the child's parent or guardian or another responsible adult, unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(5)(a)(ii)(A): the child's immediate welfare requires the child remain in protective custody; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(5)(a)(ii)(B): the protection of the community requires the child's detention in accordance with Chapter 6, Part 2, Custody and Detention.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(5)(b): 80-2a-301
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(5)(b)(i): 80-2a-301 If a peace officer or child welfare caseworker is executing a warrant under Subsection (3), the peace officer or child welfare caseworker shall take the child to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(5)(b)(i)(A): a shelter facility; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(5)(b)(i)(B): 80-2a-301 if the division makes an emergency placement under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(5)(b)(ii): If a peace officer or a child welfare caseworker takes a child to a shelter facility under Subsection (5)(b)(i), the peace officer or the child welfare caseworker shall promptly file a written report that includes the child's information, on a form provided by the division, with the shelter facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(5)(c): A child removed or taken into protective custody under this section may not be placed or kept in detention pending court proceedings, unless the child may be held in detention under Chapter 6, Part 2, Custody and Detention.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(6): 80-2a-203
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(6)(a): The juvenile court shall issue a warrant authorizing a peace officer or a child welfare worker to search for a child who is missing, has been abducted, or has run away, and take the child into physical custody if the juvenile court determines that the child is missing, has been abducted, or has run away from the protective custody, temporary custody, or custody of the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(6)(b): 80-2a-203 If the juvenile court issues a warrant under Subsection (6)(a):
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(6)(b)(i): 80-2a-203 the division shall notify the child's parent or guardian who has a right to parent-time with the child in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-202(6)(b)(ii): the court shall order:

Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304 Removal of a child from foster family placement -- Procedural due process.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(1): (1)(a); (b); 80-3-302(7)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(1)(a): The Legislature finds that, except with regard to a child's natural parent or guardian, a foster family has a very limited but recognized interest in the foster family's familial relationship with a foster child who has been in the care and custody of the foster family and in making determinations regarding removal of a child from a foster home, the division may not dismiss the foster family as a mere collection of unrelated individuals.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(1)(b): The Legislature finds that children in the temporary custody and custody of the division are experiencing multiple changes in foster care placements with little or no documentation, and that numerous studies of child growth and development emphasize the importance of stability in foster care living arrangements.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(1)(c): (1)(a); (b); 80-3-302(7) For the reasons described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(1)(c)(i): returning the child to the child's natural parent or guardian;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(1)(c)(ii): immediately placing the child in an approved adoptive home;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(1)(c)(iii): 80-3-302(7) placing the child with a relative who obtained custody or asserted an interest in the child within the preference period described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(1)(c)(iv): placing an Indian child in accordance with placement preferences and other requirements described in the Indian Child Welfare Act, 25 U.S.C. Sec. 1915.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(2): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act; (2)(a); (2)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(2)(a): Title 63G, Chapter 4, Administrative Procedures Act The division shall maintain and utilize due process procedures for removal of a foster child from a foster home, in accordance with the procedures and requirements of
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(2)(b): (2)(a) The procedures described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(2)(b)(i): personal communication with, and a written explanation of the reasons for the removal to, the foster parents before removal of the child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(2)(b)(ii): an opportunity for foster parents to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(2)(b)(ii)(A): present the foster parents' information and concerns to the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(2)(b)(ii)(B): request a review, to be held before removal of the child, by a third party neutral fact finder or if the child is placed with the foster parents for a period of at least two years, request a review, to be held before removal of the child, by the juvenile court judge currently assigned to the child's case or, if the juvenile court judge currently assigned to the child's case is not available, another juvenile court judge.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(2)(c): (2) If the division determines that there is a reasonable basis to believe that the child is in danger or that there is a substantial threat of danger to the health or welfare of the child, the division shall place the child in emergency foster care during the pendency of the procedures described in this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(3): (2); (2)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(3)(a): (2) If the division removes a child from a foster home based on the child's statement alone, the division shall initiate and expedite the processes described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(3)(b): (2) The division may not take formal action with regard to the foster parent's license until after the processes described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(4): If a complaint is made to the division by a foster child against a foster parent, the division shall, within 30 business days after the day on which the complaint is received, provide the foster parent with information regarding the specific nature of the complaint, the time and place of the alleged incident, and who was alleged to have been involved.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(5): (2); 80-3-502 If the division places a child in a foster home, the division shall provide the foster parents with:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(5)(a): notification of the requirements of this section;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(5)(b): (2) a written description of the procedures enacted by the division under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(5)(c): 80-3-502 written notification of the foster parents' ability to petition the juvenile court directly for review of a decision to remove a foster child who, subject to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(6): This section does not apply to the removal of a child based on a foster parent's request for the removal.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(7): It is unlawful for a person, with the intent to avoid compliance with the requirements of this section, to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(7)(a): take action, or encourage another to take action, against the license of a foster parent; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(7)(b): remove a child from a foster home before the child is placed with the foster parents for two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(8): The division may not remove a foster child from a foster parent who is a relative of the child on the basis of the age or health of the foster parent without determining:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(8)(a): by clear and convincing evidence that the foster parent is incapable of caring for the foster child, if the alternative foster parent would not be another relative of the child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-2a-304(8)(b): by a preponderance of the evidence that the foster parent is incapable of caring for the foster child, if the alternative foster parent would be another relative of the child.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 80 - Chapter 3 - Abuse, Neglect, and Dependency Proceedings
***************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-102(1): "Abuse, neglect, or dependency petition" means a petition filed in accordance with this chapter to commence proceedings in a juvenile court alleging that a child is:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-102(1)(a): abused;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-102(1)(b): neglected; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-102(1)(c): dependent.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-102(2): 80-2-102 "Custody" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-102(3): 80-2-201 "Division" means the Division of Child and Family Services created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-102(4): "Friend" means an adult who:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-102(4)(a): has an established relationship with the child or a family member of the child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-102(4)(b): is not the natural parent of the child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-102(5): "Immediate family member" means a spouse, child, parent, sibling, grandparent, or grandchild.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-102(6)(a): is the child's grandparent, great grandparent, aunt, great aunt, uncle, great uncle, brother-in-law, sister-in-law, stepparent, first cousin, stepsibling, or sibling;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-102(6)(b): is a first cousin of the child's parent;

Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-102(6)(d): in the case of a child who is an Indian child, is an extended family member as defined in the Indian Child Welfare Act, 25 U.S.C. Sec. 1903.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-103 Nature of proceedings -- Rules of procedure -- Ex parte communications.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-103(1): The proceedings under this chapter are civil in nature and are governed by the Utah Rules of Civil Procedure and the Utah Rules of Juvenile Procedure.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-103(2): Any unauthorized ex parte communication concerning a pending case between a judge and a party to an abuse, neglect, or dependency proceeding shall be recorded for subsequent review, if necessary, by the Judicial Conduct Commission.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-202 Expedited filing of petition.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-202(1): If an abuse, neglect, or dependency petition is requested by the division, the attorney general shall file the abuse, neglect, or dependency petition within 72 hours after the completion of the division's investigation and request, excluding weekends and holidays, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-202(1)(a): the child who is the subject of the requested abuse, neglect, or dependency petition is not removed from the child's home by the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-202(1)(b): without an expedited hearing and services ordered under the protective supervision of the juvenile court, the child will likely be taken into protective custody.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-202(2): The juvenile court shall give scheduling priority to the pretrial and adjudication hearings on an abuse, neglect, or dependency petition if:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-202(2)(a): the child who is the subject of the petition is not in:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-202(2)(a)(i): protective custody; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-202(2)(a)(ii): temporary custody; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-202(2)(b): the division indicates in the petition that, without expedited hearings and services ordered under the protective supervision of the court, the child will likely be taken into protective custody.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204 Protective custody of a child after a petition is filed -- Grounds.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(1): 80-2a-201(1); (7)(a); 80-4-104 When an abuse, neglect, or dependency petition is filed, the juvenile court shall apply, in addressing the petition, the least restrictive means and alternatives available to accomplish a compelling state interest and to prevent irretrievable destruction of family life as described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2): 80-1-102(58)(b); 80-3-109; 80-3-304; 80-4-203; Title 58, Chapter 37d, Clandestine Drug Lab Act After an abuse, neglect, or dependency petition is filed, if the child who is the subject of the petition is not in protective custody, a juvenile court may order that the child be removed from the child's home or otherwise taken into protective custody if the juvenile court finds, by a preponderance of the evidence, that any one or more of the following circumstances exist:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(a)(i): there is an imminent danger to the physical health or safety of the child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(a)(ii): the child's physical health or safety may not be protected without removing the child from the custody of the child's parent or guardian;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(b)(i): a parent or guardian engages in or threatens the child with unreasonable conduct that causes the child to suffer harm; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(b)(ii): there are no less restrictive means available by which the child's emotional health may be protected without removing the child from the custody of the child's parent or guardian;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(c): the child or another child residing in the same household has been, or is considered to be at substantial risk of being, physically abused, sexually abused, or sexually exploited, by a parent or guardian, a member of the parent's or guardian's household, or other individual known to the parent or guardian;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(d): the parent or guardian is unwilling to have physical custody of the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(e): the child is abandoned or left without any provision for the child's support;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(f): a parent or guardian who has been incarcerated or institutionalized has not arranged or cannot arrange for safe and appropriate care for the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(g): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(g)(i): a relative or other adult custodian with whom the child is left by the parent or guardian is unwilling or unable to provide care or support for the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(g)(ii): the whereabouts of the parent or guardian are unknown; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(g)(iii): reasonable efforts to locate the parent or guardian are unsuccessful;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(h): 80-1-102(58)(b); 80-3-109; 80-3-304 subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(i): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(i)(i): a parent's or guardian's actions, omissions, or habitual action create an environment that poses a serious risk to the child's health or safety for which immediate remedial or preventive action is necessary; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(i)(ii): a parent's or guardian's action in leaving a child unattended would reasonably pose a threat to the child's health or safety;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(j): the child or another child residing in the same household has been neglected;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(k): the child's natural parent:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(k)(i): intentionally, knowingly, or recklessly causes the death of another parent of the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(k)(ii): is identified by a law enforcement agency as the primary suspect in an investigation for intentionally, knowingly, or recklessly causing the death of another parent of the child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(k)(iii): is being prosecuted for or has been convicted of intentionally, knowingly, or recklessly causing the death of another parent of the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(l): 80-4-203 an infant is an abandoned infant, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(m): Title 58, Chapter 37d, Clandestine Drug Lab Act
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(m)(i): Title 58, Chapter 37d, Clandestine Drug Lab Act the parent or guardian, or an adult residing in the same household as the parent or guardian, is charged or arrested pursuant to
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(m)(ii): any clandestine laboratory operation was located in the residence or on the property where the child resided; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(2)(n): the child's welfare is otherwise endangered.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(3): (2)(a); (2)(c); (2)(c); (3)(b)(ii)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(3)(a): (2)(a) For purposes of Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(3)(b)(i): (2)(c); (3)(b)(ii) another child residing in the same household may not be removed from the home unless that child is considered to be at substantial risk of being physically abused, sexually abused, or sexually exploited as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-204(3)(b)(ii): if a parent or guardian has received actual notice that physical abuse, sexual abuse, or sexual exploitation by an individual known to the parent has occurred, and there is evidence that the parent or guardian failed to protect the child, after having received the notice, by allowing the child to be in the physical presence of the alleged abuser, that fact is prima facie evidence that the child is at substantial risk of being physically abused, sexually abused, or sexually exploited.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-205 Coordination of proceedings.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-205(1): In each case where an information or indictment is filed against a defendant concerning abuse, neglect, or dependency of a child, and a petition is filed in juvenile court concerning the victim, the appropriate county attorney's or district attorney's office shall coordinate with the attorney general's office.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-205(2): Law enforcement personnel, division personnel, the appointed guardian ad litem, pretrial services personnel, and corrections personnel shall make reasonable efforts to facilitate the coordination required under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-205(3): A member of a child protection team may participate in the coordination required under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-205(4): A member of a child protection team may coordinate with the attorney general's office, division personnel, the appointed guardian ad litem, pretrial services personnel, and corrections personnel as appropriate under this section.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-304 Second medical opinion in cases of alleged medical neglect.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-304(1): In cases of alleged medical neglect where the division seeks protective custody, temporary custody, or custody of the child based on the report or testimony of a physician, a parent or guardian shall have a reasonable amount of time, as determined by the juvenile court, to obtain a second medical opinion from another physician of the parent's or guardian's choosing who has expertise in the applicable field.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-304(2): Unless there is an imminent risk of death or a deteriorating condition of the child's health, the child shall remain in the custody of the parent or guardian while the parent or guardian obtains a second medical opinion.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-304(3): If the second medical opinion results in a different diagnosis or treatment recommendation from that of the opinion of the physician the division used, the juvenile court shall give deference to the second medical opinion as long as that opinion is reasonable and informed and is consistent with treatment that is regularly prescribed by medical experts in the applicable field.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-304(4): (1); (3) Subsections

Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-306 Outstanding arrest warrant check before return of custody.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-306(1): Before the division may recommend that a child who is in protective custody, temporary custody, or custody of the division be returned to the custody of a parent or guardian of the child, the division shall determine whether the parent or guardian has an outstanding felony arrest warrant in any state where the parent or guardian has resided or in any state where an immediate family member of the parent or guardian resides.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-306(2): The division shall file the results of the felony arrest warrant check with the juvenile court.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-306(3): (3)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-306(3)(a): If the parent or guardian of a child who is in protective custody, temporary custody, or custody of the division has an outstanding arrest warrant in any state, the juvenile court may deny the return of the child to the custody of the parent or guardian.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-401 Pretrial and adjudication hearing -- Time deadlines.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-401(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-401(1)(a): Upon the filing of an abuse, neglect, or dependency petition, the clerk of the juvenile court shall set the pretrial hearing on the petition within 15 calendar days after the later of:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-401(1)(a)(i): the day on which the shelter hearing is held; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-401(1)(a)(ii): the day on which the abuse, neglect, or dependency petition is filed.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-401(1)(b): The pretrial hearing may be continued upon motion of any party for good cause shown as described in Utah Rules of Juvenile Procedure, Rule 54.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-401(2): The final adjudication hearing shall be held no later than 60 calendar days after the later of:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-401(2)(a): the day on which the shelter hearing is held; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-401(2)(b): the day on which the abuse, neglect, or dependency petition is filed.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-402 Adjudication hearing -- Dispositional hearing time deadlines -- Scheduling of review and permanency hearing.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-402(1): If, at the adjudication hearing, the juvenile court finds, by clear and convincing evidence, that the allegations contained in the abuse, neglect, or dependency petition are true, the juvenile court shall conduct a dispositional hearing.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-402(2): (2)(c)(ii); (2)(c)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-402(2)(a): If, at the adjudication hearing, a child remains in an out-of-home placement, the juvenile court shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-402(2)(a)(i): make specific findings regarding the conditions of parent-time that are in the child's best interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-402(2)(a)(ii): if parent-time is denied, state the facts that justify the denial.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-402(2)(b): Parent-time shall be under the least restrictive conditions necessary to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-402(2)(b)(i): protect the physical safety of the child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-402(2)(b)(ii): prevent the child from being traumatized by contact with the parent due to the child's fear of the parent in light of the nature of the alleged abuse or neglect.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-402(2)(c): (2)(c)(ii); (2)(c)(i)

Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-402(2)(c)(i)(A): protect the physical safety of the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-402(2)(c)(i)(B): protect the life of the child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-402(2)(c)(i)(C): (2)(c)(ii) consistent with Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-402(2)(c)(ii)(A): the child's fear of the parent; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-402(2)(c)(ii)(B): the nature of the alleged abuse or neglect.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-402(3): The dispositional hearing may be held on the same date as the adjudication hearing, but shall be held no later than 30 calendar days after the day on which the adjudication hearing is held.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(4)(a): Because of the state's interest in and responsibility to protect and provide permanency for minors who are abused, neglected, or dependent, the Legislature finds that a parent's interest in receiving reunification services is limited.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(4)(b): The juvenile court may determine that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(4)(b)(i): efforts to reunify a minor with the minor's family are not reasonable or appropriate, based on the individual circumstances; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(4)(b)(ii): reunification services should not be provided.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(4)(c): In determining reasonable efforts to be made with respect to a minor, and in making reasonable efforts, the juvenile court and the division shall consider the minor's health, safety, and welfare as the paramount concern.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5): (6)(a); (6)(b) There is a presumption that reunification services should not be provided to a parent if the juvenile court finds, by clear and convincing evidence, that any of the following circumstances exist:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(a): the whereabouts of the parents are unknown, based on a verified affidavit indicating that a reasonably diligent search has failed to locate the parent;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(b): (6)(a) subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(c): the minor was previously adjudicated as an abused child due to physical abuse, sexual abuse, or sexual exploitation, and following the adjudication the child:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(c)(i): was removed from the custody of the minor's parent;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(c)(ii): was subsequently returned to the custody of the parent; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(c)(iii): is being removed due to additional physical abuse, sexual abuse, or sexual exploitation;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(d): the parent:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(d)(i): caused the death of another minor through abuse or neglect;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(d)(ii): committed, aided, abetted, attempted, conspired, or solicited to commit:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(d)(ii)(A): murder or manslaughter of a minor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(d)(ii)(B): child abuse homicide;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(d)(iii): committed sexual abuse against the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(d)(iv): is a registered sex offender or required to register as a sex offender; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(d)(v): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(d)(v)(A): intentionally, knowingly, or recklessly causes the death of another parent of the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(d)(v)(B): is identified by a law enforcement agency as the primary suspect in an investigation for intentionally, knowingly, or recklessly causing the death of another parent of the minor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(d)(v)(C): is being prosecuted for or has been convicted of intentionally, knowingly, or recklessly causing the death of another parent of the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(e): the minor suffered severe abuse by the parent or by any individual known by the parent if the parent knew or reasonably should have known that the individual was abusing the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(f): the minor is adjudicated as an abused minor as a result of severe abuse by the parent, and the juvenile court finds that it would not benefit the minor to pursue reunification services with the offending parent;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(g): the parent's rights are terminated with regard to any other minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(h): the minor was removed from the minor's home on at least two previous occasions and reunification services were offered or provided to the family at those times;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(i): the parent has abandoned the minor for a period of six months or longer;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(j): the parent permitted the minor to reside, on a permanent or temporary basis, at a location where the parent knew or should have known that a clandestine laboratory operation was located;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-406(5)(k): (6)(b) except as provided in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409 Permanency hearing -- Final plan -- Petition for termination of parental rights filed -- Hearing on termination of parental rights.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(1): 80-3-406
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(1)(a): 80-3-406 If reunification services are ordered under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(1)(b): If reunification services are not ordered at the dispositional hearing, the juvenile court shall hold a permanency hearing within 30 days after the day on which the dispositional hearing ends.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(2): 80-3-406
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(2)(a): 80-3-406 If reunification services are ordered in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(2)(b): If the juvenile court finds, by a preponderance of the evidence, that return of the minor to the minor's parent would create a substantial risk of detriment to the minor's physical or emotional well-being, the minor may not be returned to the custody of the minor's parent.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(2)(c): Prima facie evidence that return of the minor to a parent or guardian would create a substantial risk of detriment to the minor is established if:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(2)(c)(i): the parent or guardian fails to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(2)(c)(i)(A): participate in a court approved child and family plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(2)(c)(i)(B): comply with a court approved child and family plan in whole or in part; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(2)(c)(i)(C): meet the goals of a court approved child and family plan; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(2)(c)(ii): the minor's natural parent:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(2)(c)(ii)(A): intentionally, knowingly, or recklessly causes the death of another parent of the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(2)(c)(ii)(B): is identified by a law enforcement agency as the primary suspect in an investigation for intentionally, knowingly, or recklessly causing the death of another parent of the minor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(2)(c)(ii)(C): is being prosecuted for or has been convicted of intentionally, knowingly, or recklessly causing the death of another parent of the minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(3): 80-3-408 In making a determination under Subsection (2)(a), the juvenile court shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(3)(a): 80-3-408 review and consider:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(3)(a)(i): the report prepared by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(3)(a)(ii): in accordance with the Utah Rules of Evidence, any admissible evidence offered by the minor's attorney guardian ad litem;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(3)(a)(iii): 80-3-408 any report submitted by the division under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(3)(a)(iv): any evidence regarding the efforts or progress demonstrated by the parent; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(3)(a)(v): the extent to which the parent cooperated and used the services provided; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(3)(b): attempt to keep the minor's sibling group together if keeping the sibling group together is:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(3)(b)(i): practicable; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(3)(b)(ii): in accordance with the best interest of the minor.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(7): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(7)(a): Subject to Subsection (7)(b), the juvenile court may extend reunification services for no more than 90 days if the juvenile court finds, by a preponderance of the evidence, that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(7)(a)(i): there has been substantial compliance with the child and family plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(7)(a)(ii): reunification is probable within that 90-day period; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(7)(a)(iii): the extension is in the best interest of the minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(7)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(7)(b)(i): Except as provided in Subsection (7)(c), the juvenile court may not extend any reunification services beyond 15 months after the day on which the minor is initially removed from the minor's home.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(7)(b)(ii): Delay or failure of a parent to establish paternity or seek custody does not provide a basis for the juvenile court to extend services for the parent beyond the 12-month period described in Subsection (6).
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(7)(c): In accordance with Subsection (7)(d), the juvenile court may extend reunification services for one additional 90-day period, beyond the 90-day period described in Subsection (7)(a), if:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(7)(c)(i): the juvenile court finds, by clear and convincing evidence, that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(7)(c)(i)(A): the parent has substantially complied with the child and family plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(7)(c)(i)(B): it is likely that reunification will occur within the additional 90-day period; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(7)(c)(i)(C): the extension is in the best interest of the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(7)(c)(ii): the juvenile court specifies the facts upon which the findings described in Subsection (7)(c)(i) are based; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(7)(c)(iii): the juvenile court specifies the time period in which it is likely that reunification will occur.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(7)(d): A juvenile court may not extend the time period for reunification services without complying with the requirements of this Subsection (7) before the extension.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(7)(e): In determining whether to extend reunification services for a minor, a juvenile court shall take into consideration the status of the minor siblings of the minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(8): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(8)(a): At the permanency hearing, if a child remains in an out-of-home placement, the juvenile court shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(8)(a)(i): make specific findings regarding the conditions of parent-time that are in the child's best interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(8)(a)(ii): if parent-time is denied, state the facts that justify the denial.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(8)(b): Parent-time shall be under the least restrictive conditions necessary to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(8)(b)(i): protect the physical safety of the child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(8)(b)(ii): prevent the child from being traumatized by contact with the parent due to the child's fear of the parent in light of the nature of the alleged abuse or neglect.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(8)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(8)(c)(i): The division or the person designated by the division or a court to supervise a parent-time session may deny parent-time for the session if the division or the supervising person determines that, based on the parent's condition, it is necessary to deny parent-time to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(8)(c)(i)(A): protect the physical safety of the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(8)(c)(i)(B): protect the life of the child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(8)(c)(i)(C): consistent with Subsection (8)(c)(ii), prevent the child from being traumatized by contact with the parent.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(8)(c)(ii): In determining whether the condition of the parent described in Subsection (8)(c)(i) will traumatize a child, the division or the person supervising the parent-time session shall consider the impact that the parent's condition will have on the child in light of:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(8)(c)(ii)(A): the child's fear of the parent; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-409(8)(c)(ii)(B): the nature of the alleged abuse or neglect.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501 Placement in a qualified residential treatment program -- Review hearings.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(1)(a): "Qualified individual" means the same as that term is defined in 42 U.S.C. Sec. 675a.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(1)(b): "Qualified residential treatment program" means the same as that term is defined in 42 U.S.C. Sec. 672.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(2): Chapter 6, Juvenile Justice Within 60 days of the day on which a minor is placed in a qualified residential treatment program under this chapter or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(2)(a): review the assessment, determination, and documentation made by a qualified individual regarding the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(2)(b): determine whether the needs of the minor can be met through placement in a foster home;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(2)(c): if the minor's needs cannot be met through placement in a foster home, determine whether:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(2)(c)(i): placement of the minor in a qualified residential treatment program provides the most effective and appropriate level of care for the minor in the least restrictive environment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(2)(c)(ii): placement in a qualified residential treatment program is consistent with the short-term and long-term goals for the minor, as specified in the permanency plan for the minor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(2)(d): approve or disapprove of the minor's placement in a qualified residential treatment program.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(3): As long as a minor remains placed in a qualified residential treatment program, the juvenile court shall review the placement decision at each subsequent review and permanency hearing held with respect to the minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(4): (3) When the juvenile court conducts a review described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(4)(a): demonstrate an ongoing assessment of the strengths and needs of the minor such that the minor's needs cannot be met through placement in a foster home;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(4)(b): demonstrate that placement in a qualified residential treatment program provides the most effective and appropriate level of care for the minor in the least restrictive environment;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(4)(c): demonstrate that placement in the qualified residential treatment program is consistent with the short-term and long-term goals for the minor, as specified by the permanency plan for the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(4)(d): document the specific treatment or service needs that will be met for the minor in the placement;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(4)(e): document the length of time the minor is expected to need the treatment or services; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-501(4)(f): document the efforts made by the custodial division to prepare the minor to return home or transition to another setting, such as with a relative, with a friend of the minor, with a guardian, with an adoptive parent, a foster home, or independent living.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-502 Review of foster care removal -- Foster parent's standing.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-502(1): With regard to a minor in the custody of the division who is the subject of a petition alleging abuse, neglect, or dependency, and who has been placed in foster care with a foster family, the Legislature finds that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-502(1)(a): except with regard to the minor's natural parents, a foster family has a very limited but recognized interest in its familial relationship with the minor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-502(1)(b): minors in the custody of the division are experiencing multiple changes in foster care placements with little or no documentation, and that numerous studies of child growth and development emphasize the importance of stability in foster care living arrangements.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-502(2): (1) For the reasons described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-502(3): 80-3-302(8)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-502(3)(a): 80-3-302(8) A foster parent who has had a foster minor in the foster parent's home for 12 months or longer may petition the juvenile court for a review and determination of the appropriateness of a decision by the division to remove the minor from the foster home, unless the removal was for the purpose of:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-502(3)(a)(i): returning the minor to the minor's natural parent or legal guardian;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-502(3)(a)(ii): immediately placing the minor in an approved adoptive home;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-502(3)(a)(iii): 80-3-302(8) placing the minor with a relative who obtained custody or asserted an interest in the minor within the preference period described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-502(3)(a)(iv): placing an Indian child in accordance with placement preferences and other requirements described in the Indian Child Welfare Act, 25 U.S.C. Sec. 1915.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-502(3)(b): The foster parent may petition the juvenile court under this section without exhausting administrative remedies within the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-502(3)(c): The juvenile court may order the division to place the minor in a specified home, and shall base the juvenile court's determination on the best interest of the minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-502(4): The requirements of this section do not apply to the removal of a minor based on a foster parent's request for that removal.
