Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505 Petition for special findings for at-risk noncitizen child.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(1)(a): "At-risk" means there is reasonable cause to suspect that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(1)(a)(i): a noncitizen child's health, safety, and welfare is, or has been, in jeopardy due to abuse, neglect, abandonment, or similar circumstances; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(1)(a)(ii): the return of the noncitizen child to the noncitizen child's, or the noncitizen child's parent's, country of origin or country of last habitual residence is not in the best interest of the noncitizen child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(1)(b): "Noncitizen child" means an unmarried individual:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(1)(b)(i): who is younger than 21 years old; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(1)(b)(ii): who is not a citizen of the United States.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(1)(c): "Dependent on the court" means subject to the jurisdiction of the juvenile or district court to make decisions concerning the protection, well-being, care, and custody of a noncitizen child for findings, orders, or referrals to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(1)(c)(i): support the health, safety, and welfare of the noncitizen child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(1)(c)(ii): remedy the effects on the noncitizen child of abuse, neglect, abandonment, or similar circumstances.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(1)(d): "Similar circumstances" means a condition or conditions that have an effect on a noncitizen child comparable to abuse, neglect, or abandonment, including the death of a parent.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(2): A noncitizen child who is at-risk may petition the juvenile court for special findings regarding the abuse, neglect, abandonment, or similar circumstances of the noncitizen child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(3): (2) Upon reviewing a petition under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(3)(a): the noncitizen child:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(3)(a)(i): is dependent on the court;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(3)(a)(ii): is in the custody of the division or another appropriate person by order of the juvenile court; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(3)(a)(iii): has been appointed a guardian by a court;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(3)(b): the noncitizen child has suffered from abuse, neglect, abandonment, or similar circumstances;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(3)(c): the noncitizen child may not be viably reunified with one or both of the noncitizen child's parents due to abuse, neglect, abandonment, or similar circumstances; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(3)(d): the noncitizen child may not be returned to the noncitizen child's, or the noncitizen child's parent's, country of origin or country of last habitual residence because it is not in the best interest of the child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(4): (3)(d) In determining the best interest of the noncitizen child under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(4)(a): the health, safety, and welfare of the child to be the paramount concern for the noncitizen child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(4)(b): whether the present and past living conditions will adversely affect the noncitizen child's physical, mental, or emotional health.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(5): If the identity or location of the noncitizen child's parents is unknown or if the noncitizen child's parents reside outside the United States, the juvenile court may serve notice using any alternative method of service the court determines is appropriate or waive service.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(6): The juvenile court shall hear, adjudicate, and issue findings of fact on any petition for special findings under this section as soon as it is administratively feasible and before the noncitizen child is 21 years old.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(7): (7)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(7)(a): The juvenile court may refer a noncitizen child who is the subject of a petition for special findings under this section for psychiatric, psychological, educational, occupational, medical, dental, or social services or for protection against human trafficking or domestic violence.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(7)(b): (7)(a) A noncitizen child's participation in a referred service under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(8): This section does not:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(8)(a): limit a noncitizen child from petitioning for special findings under any other provision of law or from any other rights and remedies available to the child under any other provision of law;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(8)(b): limit the juvenile court from issuing similar findings of fact for a noncitizen child in any other proceeding concerning the noncitizen child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-3-505(8)(c): constitute an adjudication for abuse, neglect, or dependency under this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 80 - Chapter 4 - Termination and Restoration of Parental Rights
*******************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-102(1): 80-2-201 "Division" means the Division of Child and Family Services created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-102(2): "Failure of parental adjustment" means that a parent or parents are unable or unwilling within a reasonable time to substantially correct the circumstances, conduct, or conditions that led to placement of their child outside of their home, notwithstanding reasonable and appropriate efforts made by the division to return the child to the home.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-102(3): "Former parent" means an individual whose legal parental rights were terminated under this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-102(4): "Petition to restore parental rights" means a petition filed in accordance with this chapter to restore the rights of a parent with regard to a child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-102(5): "Petition for termination of parental rights" means a petition filed in accordance with this chapter to terminate the parental rights of a parent.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-102(6): 80-2-102 "Temporary custody" means the same as that term is defined in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-103 Nature of the proceedings -- Rules of procedure -- Burden of proof.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-103(1): The proceedings under this chapter are civil in nature and are governed by the Utah Rules of Civil Procedure and the Utah Rules of Juvenile Procedure.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-103(2): The juvenile court shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-103(2)(a): in all cases filed under this chapter require the petitioner to establish the facts by clear and convincing evidence;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-103(2)(b): give full and careful consideration to all of the evidence presented with regard to the constitutional rights and claims of the parent; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-103(2)(c): if a parent is found, by reason of the parent's conduct or condition, to be unfit or incompetent based upon any of the grounds for termination described in this chapter, consider the welfare and best interest of the child of paramount importance in determining whether to terminate parental rights.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104 Judicial process for termination -- Parent unfit or incompetent -- Best interest of child.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(1): Under both the United States Constitution and the constitution of this state, a parent possesses a fundamental liberty interest in the care, custody, and management of the parent's child.  For this reason, the termination of family ties by the state may only be done for compelling reasons.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(2): The juvenile court shall provide a fundamentally fair process to a parent if a party moves to terminate the parent's parental rights.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(3): If the party moving to terminate parental rights is a governmental entity, the juvenile court shall find that any actions or allegations made in opposition to the rights and desires of a parent regarding the parent's child are supported by sufficient evidence to satisfy a parent's constitutional entitlement to heightened protection against government interference with the parent's fundamental rights and liberty interests.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(4)(a): The fundamental liberty interest of a parent concerning the care, custody, and management of the parent's child is recognized, protected, and does not cease to exist simply because:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(4)(a)(i): a parent may fail to be a model parent; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(4)(a)(ii): the parent's child is placed in the temporary custody of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(4)(b): The juvenile court should give serious consideration to the fundamental right of a parent to rear the parent's child, and concomitantly, of the right of the child to be reared by the child's natural parent.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(5): At all times, a parent retains a vital interest in preventing the irretrievable destruction of family life.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(6): Before an adjudication of unfitness, government action in relation to a parent and a parent's child may not exceed the least restrictive means or alternatives available to accomplish a compelling state interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(7): Until parental unfitness is established and the children suffer, or are substantially likely to suffer, serious detriment as a result, the child and the child's parent share a vital interest in preventing erroneous termination of their relationship and the juvenile court may not presume that a child and the child's parents are adversaries.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(8): It is in the best interest and welfare of a child to be raised under the care and supervision of the child's natural parents. A child's need for a normal family life in a permanent home, and for positive, nurturing family relationships is usually best met by the child's natural parents. Additionally, the integrity of the family unit and the right of parents to conceive and raise their children are constitutionally protected. For these reasons, the juvenile court should only transfer custody of a child from the child's natural parent for compelling reasons and when there is a jurisdictional basis to do so.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(9): The right of a fit, competent parent to raise the parent's child without undue government interference is a fundamental liberty interest that has long been protected by the laws and Constitution of this state and of the United States, and is a fundamental public policy of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(10): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(10)(a): The state recognizes that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(10)(a)(i): a parent has the right, obligation, responsibility, and authority to raise, manage, train, educate, provide for, and reasonably discipline the parent's child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(10)(a)(ii): the state's role is secondary and supportive to the primary role of a parent.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(10)(b): It is the public policy of this state that a parent retain the fundamental right and duty to exercise primary control over the care, supervision, upbringing, and education of the parent's child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(10)(c): The interests of the state favor preservation and not severance of natural familial bonds in situations where a positive, nurturing parent-child relationship can exist, including extended family association and support.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(11): This chapter provides a judicial process for voluntary and involuntary severance of the parent-child relationship, designed to safeguard the rights and interests of all parties concerned and promote their welfare and that of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(12): 80-4-301; 80-3-302
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(12)(a): Wherever possible, family life should be strengthened and preserved, but if a parent is found, by reason of the parent's conduct or condition, to be unfit or incompetent based upon any of the grounds for termination described in this part, the juvenile court shall then consider the welfare and best interest of the child of paramount importance in determining whether termination of parental rights shall be ordered.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(12)(b): 80-4-301; 80-3-302 In determining whether termination is in the best interest of the child, and in finding, based on the totality of the circumstances, that termination of parental rights, from the child's point of view, is strictly necessary to promote the child's best interest, the juvenile court shall consider, among other relevant factors, whether:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(12)(b)(i): 80-4-301 sufficient efforts were dedicated to reunification in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-104(12)(b)(ii): 80-3-302 pursuant to Section


Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-105 Effect of decree.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-105(1): An order for the termination of parental rights divests the child and the parents of all legal rights, powers, immunities, duties, and obligations with respect to each other, except the right of the child to inherit from the parent.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-105(2): An order or decree entered under this chapter may not disentitle a child to any benefit due to the child from any third person, including any Indian tribe, agency, state, or the United States.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-105(3): 80-4-401; 80-4-402 Except as provided in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-105(3)(a): is not entitled to any notice of proceedings for the adoption of the child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-105(3)(b): does not have any right to object to the adoption or to participate in any other placement proceedings.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-105(4): An order terminating the rights of a parent, guardian, or custodian does not expire with termination of the jurisdiction of the juvenile court.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-201 Petition -- Who may file -- Dismissal.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-201(1): Any interested party, including a foster parent, may file a petition for termination of parental rights.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-201(2): The attorney general shall file a petition for termination of parental rights under this chapter on behalf of the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-201(3): The juvenile court may dismiss a petition for termination of parental rights at any stage of the proceedings.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301 Grounds for termination of parental rights -- Findings regarding reasonable efforts by division.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1): 80-4-104; 77-37-2 Subject to the protections and requirements of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(a): the parent has abandoned the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(b): the parent has neglected or abused the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(c): the parent is unfit or incompetent;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(d): 77-37-2
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(d)(i): 77-37-2 the parent was convicted of a sexual offense, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(d)(ii): the offense resulted in the conception of the child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(d)(iii): termination is in the best interest of the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(e): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(e)(i): the child is being cared for in an out-of-home placement under the supervision of the juvenile court or the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(e)(ii): the parent has substantially neglected, willfully refused, or has been unable or unwilling to remedy the circumstances that cause the child to be in an out-of-home placement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(e)(iii): there is a substantial likelihood that the parent will not be capable of exercising proper and effective parental care in the near future;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(f): failure of parental adjustment, as defined in this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(g): only token efforts have been made by the parent:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(g)(i): to support or communicate with the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(g)(ii): to prevent neglect of the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(g)(iii): to eliminate the risk of serious harm to the child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(g)(iv): to avoid being an unfit parent;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(h): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(h)(i): the parent has voluntarily relinquished the parent's parental rights to the child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(h)(ii): termination is in the child's best interest;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(i): after a period of trial during which the child was returned to live in the child's own home, the parent substantially and continuously or repeatedly refused or failed to give the child proper parental care and protection; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(1)(j): the terms and conditions of safe relinquishment of a newborn child have been complied with as described in Part 5, Safe Relinquishment of a Newborn Child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(2): 80-4-303; 80-4-304 When determining whether termination of parental rights is strictly necessary to promote the child's best interest, the court shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(2)(a): undertake the analysis from the child's point of view;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(2)(b): focus on finding the outcome that best secures the child's well-being;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(2)(c): 80-4-303; 80-4-304 include, as applicable, the considerations described in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(2)(d): explore whether other feasible options exist that could address the specific problems or issues facing the family, short of imposing the ultimate remedy of terminating the parent's rights.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(3): The juvenile court may not terminate the parental rights of a parent because the parent has failed to complete the requirements of a child and family plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(4)(a): Except as provided in Subsection (4)(b), in any case in which the juvenile court has directed the division to provide reunification services to a parent, the juvenile court must find that the division made reasonable efforts to provide those services before the juvenile court may terminate the parent's rights under Subsection (1)(b), (c), (e), (f), (g), or (i).
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(4)(b): Notwithstanding Subsection (4)(a), the juvenile court is not required to make the finding under Subsection (4)(a) before terminating a parent's rights:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(4)(b)(i): under Subsection (1)(b), if the juvenile court finds that the abuse or neglect occurred subsequent to adjudication; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-301(4)(b)(ii): if reasonable efforts to provide the services described in Subsection (4)(a) are not required under federal law, and federal law is not inconsistent with Utah law.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302 Evidence of grounds for termination.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(1): 80-4-203 In determining whether a parent or parents have abandoned a child, it is prima facie evidence of abandonment that the parent or parents:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(1)(a): although having legal custody of the child, have surrendered physical custody of the child, and for a period of six months following the surrender have not manifested to the child or to the person having the physical custody of the child a firm intention to resume physical custody or to make arrangements for the care of the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(1)(b): have failed to communicate with the child by mail, telephone, or otherwise for six months;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(1)(c): failed to have shown the normal interest of a natural parent, without just cause; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(1)(d): 80-4-203 have abandoned an infant, as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(2): 76-10-1201 In determining whether a parent or parents are unfit or have neglected a child the juvenile court shall consider:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(2)(a): emotional illness, mental illness, or mental deficiency of the parent that renders the parent unable to care for the immediate and continuing physical or emotional needs of the child for extended periods of time;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(2)(b): conduct toward a child of a physically, emotionally, or sexually cruel or abusive nature;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(2)(c): habitual or excessive use of intoxicating liquors, controlled substances, or dangerous drugs that render the parent unable to care for the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(2)(d): repeated or continuous failure to provide the child with adequate food, clothing, shelter, education, or other care necessary for the child's physical, mental, and emotional health and development by a parent or parents who are capable of providing that care;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(2)(e): whether the parent is incarcerated as a result of conviction of a felony, and the sentence is of such length that the child will be deprived of a normal home for more than one year;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(2)(f): a history of violent behavior;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(2)(g): 76-10-1201 whether the parent has intentionally exposed the child to pornography or material harmful to a minor, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(2)(h): any other circumstance, conduct, or condition that the court considers relevant in the determination of whether a parent or parents are unfit or have neglected the child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(3): (2)(c); 26B-4-201; Title 26B, Chapter 4, Part 2, Cannabinoid Research and Medical Cannabis Notwithstanding Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(4): A parent who, legitimately practicing the parent's religious beliefs, does not provide specified medical treatment for a child is not, for that reason alone, a negligent or unfit parent.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(5): (2); (5)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(5)(a): (2) Notwithstanding Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(5)(b): (5)(a) Nothing in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(6): If a child has been placed in the custody of the division and the parent or parents fail to comply substantially with the terms and conditions of a plan within six months after the date on which the child was placed or the plan was commenced, whichever occurs later, that failure to comply is evidence of failure of parental adjustment.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(7): The following circumstances are prima facie evidence of unfitness:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(7)(a): sexual abuse, sexual exploitation, injury, or death of a sibling of the child, or of any child, due to known or substantiated abuse or neglect by the parent or parents;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(7)(b): conviction of a crime, if the facts surrounding the crime are of such a nature as to indicate the unfitness of the parent to provide adequate care to the extent necessary for the child's physical, mental, or emotional health and development;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(7)(c): a single incident of life-threatening or gravely disabling injury to or disfigurement of the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(7)(d): the parent has committed, aided, abetted, attempted, conspired, or solicited to commit murder or manslaughter of a child or child abuse homicide; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-302(7)(e): the parent intentionally, knowingly, or recklessly causes the death of another parent of the child, without legal justification.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-303 Specific considerations when child is not in physical custody of parent.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-303(1): If a child is not in the physical custody of the child's parent or parents, the juvenile court, in determining whether parental rights should be terminated, shall consider:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-303(1)(a): the physical, mental, or emotional condition and needs of the child and the child's desires regarding the termination, if the juvenile court determines the child is of sufficient capacity to express the child's desires;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-303(1)(b): the effort the child's parent or parents have made to adjust the parent's or parents' circumstances, conduct, or conditions to make it in the child's best interest to return the child to the child's home after a reasonable length of time, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-303(1)(b)(i): payment of a reasonable portion of substitute physical care and maintenance, if financially able;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-303(1)(b)(ii): maintenance of regular parent-time or other contact with the child that was designed and carried out in a plan to reunite the child with the parent or parents; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-303(1)(b)(iii): maintenance of regular contact and communication with the custodian of the child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-303(1)(c): any other factor that the juvenile court considers relevant in the determination of whether to terminate parental rights.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-303(2): For purposes of this section, the juvenile court shall disregard incidental conduct, contributions, contacts, and communications.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-304 Specific considerations when child is placed in foster home.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If a child is in the custody of the division and has been placed and resides in a foster home and the division institutes proceedings under this chapter regarding the child, with an ultimate goal of having the child's foster parent or parents adopt the child, the juvenile court shall consider:Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-304(1): whether the child has become integrated into the foster family to the extent that the child's familial identity is with the foster family;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-304(2): whether the foster family is able and willing permanently to treat the child as a member of the family;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-304(3): the love, affection, and other emotional ties existing between the child and the parents, and the child's ties with the foster family;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-304(4): the capacity and disposition of the child's parents from whom the child was removed as compared with that of the foster family to give the child love, affection, and guidance and to continue the education of the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-304(5): the length of time the child has lived in a stable, satisfactory foster home and the desirability of the child continuing to live in that environment;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-304(6): the permanence as a family unit of the foster family; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-304(7): any other factor that the juvenile court considers relevant to a particular placement of a child.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305 Court disposition of child upon termination of parental rights -- Posttermination reunification.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(1): (7) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(1)(a): an adult who is a grandparent, great-grandparent, aunt, great aunt, uncle, great uncle, brother-in-law, sister-in-law, stepparent, first cousin, sibling, or stepsibling of a child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(1)(b): in the case of a child who is an Indian child, an extended family member as defined in the Indian Child Welfare Act, 25 U.S.C. Sec. 1903.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(2): 80-3-405 Upon entry of an order under this chapter, the juvenile court may:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(2)(a): place the child in the legal custody and guardianship of a child-placing agency or the division for adoption; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(2)(b): 80-3-405 make any other disposition of the child authorized under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(3): (4); (6) Subject to Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(4): If the parental rights of all parents of an adoptable child placed in the custody of the division are terminated and a suitable adoptive placement is not already available, the juvenile court:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(4)(a): shall determine whether there is a relative who desires to adopt the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(4)(b): may order the division to conduct a reasonable search to determine whether there is a relative who is willing to adopt the child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(4)(c): shall, if a relative desires to adopt the child:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(4)(c)(i): make a specific finding regarding the fitness of the relative to adopt the child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(4)(c)(ii): place the child for adoption with the relative unless the juvenile court finds that adoption by the relative is not in the best interest of the child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(5): 80-3-302(7)(a)(i) If an individual who is not a relative of the child desires to adopt the child, the juvenile court shall, before entering an order for adoption of the child, determine whether due weight was given to the relative's preferential consideration under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(6): This section does not guarantee that a relative will be permitted to adopt the child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(7): 80-3-102 A parent whose rights are terminated under this chapter, or a relative of the child, as defined by Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(7)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(7)(a)(i): following an adoptive placement, the child's adoptive parent returns the child to the custody of the division; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(7)(a)(ii): the child is in the custody of the division for one year following the day on which the parent's rights were terminated, and no permanent placement has been found or is likely to be found; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-305(7)(b): reunification with the child's parent, or guardianship by the child's relative, is in the best interest of the child.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-306 Review following termination.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-306(1): At the conclusion of the hearing in which the juvenile court orders termination of parental rights, the juvenile court shall order that a review hearing be held within 90 days after the day on which parental rights are terminated if the child has not been permanently placed.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-306(2): (1) At the review hearing described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-306(2)(a): the agency or individual vested with custody of the child shall report to the juvenile court regarding the plan for permanent placement of the child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-306(2)(b): the guardian ad litem shall make recommendations to the juvenile court, based on an independent investigation, for disposition meeting the best interests of the child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-306(3): The juvenile court may order the agency or individual vested with custody of the child to report, at appropriate intervals, on the status of the child until the plan for permanent placement of the child is accomplished.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-307 Voluntary relinquishment -- Irrevocable.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-307(1): 78B-6-124 The individual consenting to termination of parental rights or voluntarily relinquishing parental rights shall sign the consent or relinquishment, or confirm a consent or relinquishment previously signed by the individual, under oath before:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-307(1)(a): a judge of any court that has jurisdiction over proceedings for termination of parental rights in this state or any other state, or a public officer appointed by that court for the purpose of taking consents or relinquishments; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-307(1)(b): 78B-6-124 except as provided in Subsection (2), any person authorized to take consents or relinquishments under Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-307(2): Only the juvenile court is authorized to take consents or relinquishments from a parent who has any child who is in the custody of a state agency or who has a child who is otherwise under the jurisdiction of the juvenile court.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-307(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-307(3)(a): The court, appointed officer, or other authorized person shall certify to the best of that person's information and belief that the individual executing the consent or relinquishment, or confirming a consent or relinquishment previously signed by the individual, has read and understands the consent or relinquishment and has signed the consent or relinquishment freely and voluntarily.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-307(3)(b): A consent or relinquishment is not effective until the consent or relinquishment is certified pursuant to Subsection (3)(a).
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-307(4): A consent or relinquishment that has been certified pursuant to Subsection (3)(a) is effective against the consenting or relinquishing individual and may not be revoked.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-307(5): 80-4-104; 80-4-301; 80-4-304
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-307(5)(a): 80-4-104; 80-4-301; 80-4-304 The requirements and processes described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-307(5)(b): When determining voluntary relinquishment or consent for termination of parental rights, the juvenile court need only find that the relinquishment or termination is in the child's best interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-307(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-307(6)(a): There is a presumption that voluntary relinquishment or consent for termination of parental rights is not in the child's best interest where it appears to the juvenile court that the primary purpose for relinquishment or consent for termination is to avoid a financial support obligation.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-307(6)(b): The presumption described in Subsection (6)(a) may be rebutted if the juvenile court finds the relinquishment or consent to termination of parental rights will facilitate the establishment of stability and permanency for the child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-307(7): Upon granting a voluntary relinquishment the juvenile court may make orders relating to the child's care and welfare that the juvenile court considers to be in the child's best interest.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401 Petition to restore parental rights -- Division duties.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(1): A child, who is 12 years old or older, or an authorized representative acting on behalf of a child of any age, may file a petition to restore parental rights if:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(1)(a): 24 months have passed since the day on which the juvenile court ordered termination of the former parent's parental rights; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(1)(b): the child:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(1)(b)(i): has not been adopted and is not in an adoptive placement, or is unlikely to be adopted before the child is 18 years old; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(1)(b)(ii): was previously adopted following a termination of parental rights, but the adoption failed and the child was returned to the custody of the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(2): The petition to restore parental rights shall be:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(2)(a): filed in the juvenile court that previously terminated parental rights; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(2)(b): served on the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(3): (1) The division shall notify and inform a child who is 12 years old or older and who qualifies for restoration of parental rights under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(4): (4)(a) Upon the receipt of a petition to restore parental rights, filed by a child or an authorized representative acting on behalf of a child, the division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(4)(a): make a diligent effort to locate the former parent whose rights may be restored under this part; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(4)(b): (4)(a) if the former parent is found, as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(4)(b)(i): the legal effects of restoration; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(4)(b)(ii): the time and date of the hearing on the petition to restore parental rights.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(5): The juvenile court shall set a hearing on the petition to restore parental rights at least 30 days, but no more than 60 days, after the day on which the petition to restore parental rights is filed with the juvenile court.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(6): (5) Before the hearing described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(6)(a): material changes in circumstances since the termination of parental rights;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(6)(b): a summary of the reasons why parental rights were terminated;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(6)(c): the date on which parental rights were terminated;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(6)(d): the willingness of the former parent to resume contact with the child and have parental rights restored;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(6)(e): the ability of the former parent to be involved in the life of the child and accept physical custody of, and responsibility for, the child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(6)(f): any other information the division reasonably considers appropriate and determinative.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(7): (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(7)(a): (1) A former parent who remedies the circumstances that resulted in the termination of the former parent's parental rights and who is capable of exercising proper and effective parental care, shall notify the division that if the circumstances described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-401(7)(b): The former parent's request to the division shall be fully and fairly considered by the division for appropriate submittal to the court.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402 Hearing on petition to restore parental rights.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(1): 80-4-401(1) The juvenile court may restore a parent's parental rights if:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(1)(a): 80-4-401(1) the child meets the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(1)(b): considering the age and maturity of the child, the child consents to the restoration;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(1)(c): the former parent consents to the restoration; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(1)(d): the juvenile court finds by clear and convincing evidence that restoration is in the best interest of the child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(2): In determining whether reunification under this section is appropriate and in the best interest of the child, the juvenile court shall consider:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(2)(a): whether the former parent has been sufficiently rehabilitated from the behavior that resulted in the termination of parental rights;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(2)(b): extended family support for the former parent; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(2)(c): other material changes of circumstances, if any, that may have occurred that warrant the granting of the motion.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(3): At the hearing on a petition to restore parental rights, if the former parent consents and if the juvenile court finds by clear and convincing evidence that it is in the best interest of the child, the juvenile court may:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(3)(a): allow contact between the former parent and the child, and describe the conditions under which contact may take place;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(3)(b): order that the child be placed with the former parent, in a temporary custody and guardianship relationship, to be reevaluated after the child has been placed with the former parent for six months; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(3)(c): restore the parental rights of the parent.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(4): (3) If the juvenile court orders the child to be placed in the physical custody of the former parent under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(4)(a): whether that custody is subject to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(4)(a)(i): continued evaluation by the court; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(4)(a)(ii): the supervision of the division; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-402(4)(b): the terms and conditions of reunification.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-501 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-501(1): 26B-2-201 "Hospital" means a general acute hospital, as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-501(1)(a): equipped with an emergency room;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-501(1)(b): open 24 hours a day, seven days a week; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-501(1)(c): employs full-time health care professionals who have emergency medical services training.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-501(2): "Newborn child" means a child who is approximately 30 days old or younger, as determined within a reasonable degree of medical certainty.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502 Safe relinquishment of a newborn child -- Termination of parental rights -- Affirmative defense.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(1)(a): A parent or a parent's designee may safely relinquish a newborn child at a hospital in accordance with this part and retain complete anonymity, so long as the newborn child has not been subject to abuse or neglect.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(1)(b): Safe relinquishment of a newborn child who has not otherwise been subject to abuse or neglect shall not, in and of itself, constitute neglect, and the newborn child may not be considered a neglected child so long as the relinquishment is carried out in substantial compliance with this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(2): (2)(b)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(2)(a): Personnel employed by a hospital shall accept a newborn child who is relinquished under this part, and may presume that the individual relinquishing is the newborn child's parent or the parent's designee.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(2)(b): The person receiving the newborn child may request information regarding the parent and newborn child's medical histories, and identifying information regarding the nonrelinquishing parent of the newborn child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(2)(c): (2)(b) If the newborn child's parent or the parent's designee provides the person receiving the newborn child with any of the information described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(2)(d): Personnel employed by the hospital shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(2)(d)(i): provide any necessary medical care to the newborn child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(2)(d)(ii): notify the division of receipt of the newborn child as soon as possible, but no later than 24 hours after receipt of the newborn child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(2)(d)(iii): prepare a birth certificate or foundling birth certificate if parentage is unknown for the newborn child and file the certificate with the Office of Vital Records and Statistics within the Department of Health.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(2)(e): A hospital and personnel employed by a hospital are immune from any civil or criminal liability arising from accepting a newborn child if the personnel employed by the hospital substantially comply with the provisions of this part and medical treatment is administered according to standard medical practice.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(3): The division shall assume care and protective custody of the newborn child immediately upon notice from the hospital.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(4): 80-2-701; Chapter 3, Abuse, Neglect, and Dependency Proceedings So long as the division determines there is no abuse or neglect of the newborn child, neither the newborn child nor the child's parents are subject to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(4)(a): 80-2-701 the investigation provisions contained in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(4)(b): Chapter 3, Abuse, Neglect, and Dependency Proceedings the provisions of
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(5): Title 78B, Chapter 15, Part 4, Registry; (5)(a)(iii); Title 78B, Chapter 15, Part 4, Registry; (5)(a)(iv); 80-4-301
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(5)(a): Title 78B, Chapter 15, Part 4, Registry; (5)(a)(iii); Title 78B, Chapter 15, Part 4, Registry Unless identifying information relating to the nonrelinquishing parent of the newborn child is provided, the division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(5)(a)(i): work with local law enforcement and the Bureau of Criminal Identification within the Department of Public Safety in an effort to ensure that the newborn child has not been identified as a missing child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(5)(a)(ii): immediately place or contract for placement of the newborn child in a potential adoptive home and, within 10 days after the day on which the child is received, file a petition for termination of parental rights in accordance with this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(5)(a)(iii): Title 78B, Chapter 15, Part 4, Registry direct the Office of Vital Records and Statistics within the Department of Health to conduct a search for:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(5)(a)(iii)(A): a birth certificate for the newborn child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(5)(a)(iii)(B): Title 78B, Chapter 15, Part 4, Registry unmarried biological fathers in the registry maintained by the Office of Vital Records and Statistics in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(5)(a)(iv): (5)(a)(iii); Title 78B, Chapter 15, Part 4, Registry provide notice to each potential father identified on the registry described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(5)(b): (5)(a)(iv); 80-4-301
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(5)(b)(i): (5)(a)(iv) If no individual has affirmatively identified himself or herself within two weeks after the day on which notice under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(5)(b)(ii): 80-4-301 If a nonrelinquishing parent is not identified, relinquishment of a newborn child under this part is considered grounds for termination of parental rights of both the relinquishing and nonrelinquishing parents under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(6): If at any time before the day on which the newborn child is adopted, the juvenile court finds it is in the best interest of the newborn child, the court shall deny the petition for termination of parental rights.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(7): The division shall provide for, or contract with a child-placing agency to provide for expeditious adoption of the newborn child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-4-502(8): So long as the individual relinquishing a newborn child is the newborn child's parent or designee, and there is no abuse or neglect, safe relinquishment of a newborn child in substantial compliance with this part is an affirmative defense to any potential criminal liability for abandonment or neglect relating to the relinquishment.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 80 - Chapter 5 - Juvenile Justice Services

-------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-103 Creation of division -- Jurisdiction.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-103(1): There is created the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services within the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-103(2): The division shall be under the administration and supervision of the executive director of the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-103(3): 80-6-703; 80-6-705 The division has jurisdiction over all minors committed to the division under Sections


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-104 Division director -- Qualifications -- Responsibility.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-104(1): The executive director of the department shall appoint the director of the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-104(2): The director shall have a bachelor's degree from an accredited university or college, be experienced in administration, and be knowledgeable in juvenile justice.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-104(3): The director is the administrative head of the division.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201 Division responsibilities.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(1): 80-6-703; 80-6-705 The division is responsible for all minors committed to the division by juvenile courts under Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2): 80-6-706; 80-6-703; 53-10-403; 77-41-102; 77-41-102; 63M-7-208 The division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(a): establish and administer a continuum of community, secure, and nonsecure programs for all minors committed to the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(b): establish and maintain all detention and secure care facilities and set minimum standards for all detention and secure care facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(c): establish and operate prevention and early intervention youth services programs for nonadjudicated minors placed with the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(d): 80-6-706 establish observation and assessment programs necessary to serve minors in a nonresidential setting under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(e): 80-6-703 place minors committed to the division under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(f): employ staff necessary to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(f)(i): supervise and control minors committed to the division for secure care or placement in the community;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(f)(ii): supervise and coordinate treatment of minors committed to the division for placement in community-based programs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(f)(iii): control and supervise adjudicated and nonadjudicated minors placed with the division for temporary services in juvenile receiving centers, youth services, and other programs established by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(g): control or detain a minor committed to the division, or in the temporary custody of the division, in a manner that is consistent with public safety and rules made by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(h): establish and operate work programs for minors committed to the division by the juvenile court that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(h)(i): are not residential;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(h)(ii): provide labor to help in the operation, repair, and maintenance of public facilities, parks, highways, and other programs designated by the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(h)(iii): provide educational and prevocational programs in cooperation with the State Board of Education for minors placed in the program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(h)(iv): provide counseling to minors;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(i): establish minimum standards for the operation of all private residential and nonresidential rehabilitation facilities that provide services to minors who have committed an offense in this state or in any other state;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(j): provide regular training for secure care staff, detention staff, case management staff, and staff of the community-based programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(k): 53-10-403 designate employees to obtain the saliva DNA specimens required under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(l): ensure that the designated employees receive appropriate training and that the specimens are obtained in accordance with accepted protocol;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(m): 77-41-102; 77-41-102 register an individual with the Department of Public Safety who:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(m)(i): 77-41-102; 77-41-102 is adjudicated for an offense listed in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(m)(ii): is committed to the division for secure care; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(m)(iii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(m)(iii)(A): if the individual is a youth offender, remains in the division's custody 30 days before the individual's 21st birthday; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(m)(iii)(B): if the individual is a serious youth offender, remains in the division's custody 30 days before the individual's 25th birthday; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(2)(n): 63M-7-208 ensure that a program delivered to a minor under this section is an evidence-based program in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(3): 53-13-105
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(3)(a): 53-13-105 The division is authorized to employ special function officers, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(3)(a)(i): locate and apprehend minors who have absconded from division custody;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(3)(a)(ii): transport minors taken into custody in accordance with division policy;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(3)(a)(iii): investigate cases; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(3)(a)(iv): carry out other duties as assigned by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(3)(b): A special function officer may be:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(3)(b)(i): employed through a contract with the Department of Public Safety, or any law enforcement agency certified by the Peace Officer Standards and Training Division; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(3)(b)(ii): directly hired by the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(4): In the event of an unauthorized leave from secure care, detention, a community-based program, a juvenile receiving center, a home, or any other designated placement of a minor, a division employee has the authority and duty to locate and apprehend the minor, or to initiate action with a local law enforcement agency for assistance.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-201(5): The division may proceed with an initial medical screening or assessment of a child admitted to a detention facility to ensure the safety of the child and others in the detention facility if the division makes a good faith effort to obtain consent for the screening or assessment from the child's parent or guardian.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202 Division rulemaking authority -- Reports on sexual assault.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(1): 80-6-704; 80-6-809 In accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, the division shall make rules to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(1)(a): establish standards for the admission of a minor to detention;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(1)(b): 80-6-704 describe good behavior for which credit may be earned under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(1)(c): establish a formula, in consultation with the Office of the Legislative Fiscal Analyst, to calculate savings from General Fund appropriations under 2017 Laws of Utah,
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(1)(d): establish policies and procedures regarding sexual assaults that occur in detention and secure care facilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(1)(e): 80-6-809 establish the qualifications and conditions for services provided by the division under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(2): 80-5-401 In accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, the division may make rules:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(2)(a): 80-5-401 that govern the operation of prevention and early intervention programs, youth service programs, juvenile receiving centers, and other programs described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(2)(b): that govern the operation of detention and secure care facilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(3): A rule made by the division under Subsection (1)(a):
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(3)(a): may not permit secure detention based solely on the existence of multiple status offenses, misdemeanors, or infractions arising out of a single criminal episode; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(3)(b): shall prioritize use of home detention for a minor who might otherwise be held in secure detention.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4): The rules described in Subsection (1)(d) shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(a): require education and training, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(a)(i): providing to minors detained in secure care and detention facilities, at intake and periodically, easy-to-understand information, which is developed and approved by the division, on sexual assault prevention, treatment, reporting, and counseling in consultation with community groups with expertise in sexual assault prevention, treatment, reporting, and counseling; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(a)(ii): providing training specific to sexual assault to division mental health professionals and all division employees who have direct contact with minors regarding treatment and methods of prevention and investigation;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(b): require reporting of any incident of sexual assault, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(b)(i): ensuring the confidentiality of sexual assault reports from minors and the protection of minors who report sexual assault; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(b)(ii): prohibiting retaliation and disincentives for reporting sexual assault;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(c): require safety and care for minors who report sexual assault, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(c)(i): providing, in situations in which there is reason to believe that a sexual assault has occurred, reasonable and appropriate measures to ensure the minor's safety by separating the minor from the minor's assailant, if known;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(c)(ii): providing acute trauma care for minors who report sexual assault, including treatment of injuries, HIV prophylaxis measures, and testing for sexually transmitted infections;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(c)(iii): providing confidential mental health counseling for minors who report sexual assault, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(c)(iii)(A): access to outside community groups or victim advocates that have expertise in sexual assault counseling; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(c)(iii)(B): enabling confidential communication between minors and community groups and victim advocates; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(c)(iv): monitoring minors who report sexual assault for suicidal impulses, post-traumatic stress disorder, depression, and other mental health consequences resulting from the sexual assault;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(d): require staff reporting of sexual assault and staff discipline for failure to report or for violating sexual assault policies, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(d)(i): requiring all division employees to report any knowledge, suspicion, or information regarding an incident of sexual assault to the director or the director's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(d)(ii): requiring disciplinary action for a division employee who fails to report as required; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(d)(iii): requiring division employees to be subject to disciplinary sanctions up to and including termination for violating agency sexual assault policies, with termination the presumptive disciplinary sanction for division employees who have engaged in sexual assault, consistent with constitutional due process protections and state personnel laws and rules;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(e): require that any report of an incident of sexual assault be referred to the Division of Child and Family Services or a law enforcement agency with jurisdiction over the detention or secure care facility in which the alleged sexual assault occurred; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(4)(f): require data collection and reporting of all incidents of sexual assault from each detention and secure care facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-202(5): The division shall annually report the data described in Section (4)(f) to the Law Enforcement and Criminal Justice Interim Committee.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-203 Detention risk assessment tool.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-203(1): The division, in conjunction with the Administrative Office of the Courts, shall develop or adopt, and validate on the Utah juvenile population, a statewide detention risk assessment tool.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-203(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-203(2)(a): The division shall administer the detention risk assessment tool for each minor under consideration for detention.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-203(2)(b): A designated individual who has completed training to conduct the detention risk assessment tool shall administer the detention risk assessment tool.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-203(3): The division and the Administrative Office of the Courts shall establish a scoring system to inform eligibility  for placement of a minor in a detention facility or for referral to an alternative to detention.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-204 Annual review of programs and facilities.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-204(1): (1)(a)(i); (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-204(1)(a): (1)(a)(i) The division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-204(1)(a)(i): annually review all programs and facilities that provide services to minors who have committed an offense, in this state or in any other state, which would constitute a felony or misdemeanor if committed by an adult; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-204(1)(a)(ii): (1)(a)(i) license all programs and facilities under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-204(1)(b): (1)(a) The division shall provide a written review to the manager of a program or facility under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-204(1)(c): A program or facility that is unable or unwilling to comply with the standards  established by the division  may not be licensed.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-204(2): Any private facility or program providing services under this chapter that willfully fails to comply with the standards established by the division is guilty of a class B misdemeanor.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-205 Contracts with private providers.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-205(1): This chapter does not prohibit the division from contracting with private providers or other agencies for:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-205(1)(a): the construction, operation, and maintenance of juvenile facilities; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-205(1)(b): the provision of care, treatment, and supervision of minors who have been committed to the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-205(2): All programs for the care, treatment, and supervision of minors committed to the division shall be licensed in compliance with division standards within six months after commencing operation.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-205(3): 63M-7-208 A contract for the care, treatment, and supervision of a minor committed to the division shall be executed in accordance with the performance-based contracting system developed under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-206 Records -- Property of division.
---------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-206(1): All records maintained by programs that are under contract with the division to provide services to minors, are the property of the division and shall be returned to the division when the minor is terminated from the program.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-206(2): The division shall maintain an accurate audit trail of information provided to other programs or agencies regarding minors under the division's jurisdiction.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-207 Restitution by a minor committed to the division.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-207(1): (1)(c)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-207(1)(a): The division shall make reasonable efforts to ensure that restitution is made to the victim of a minor who is committed to the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-207(1)(b): (1)(c) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-207(1)(c): Reimbursement to the victim of a minor is conditional upon the minor's involvement in the work program.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-207(2): The division shall notify the juvenile court of all restitution paid to victims through the employment of a minor, who is committed to the division, in a work program.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-208 Care of pregnant minor in secure detention or secure care.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-208(1): When a minor in secure detention or secure care is pregnant, the division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-208(1)(a): ensure that adequate prenatal and postnatal care is provided; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-208(1)(b): place the minor in an accredited hospital before delivery.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-208(2): As soon as the minor's condition after delivery will permit, the minor may be returned to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-208(2)(a): secure detention if the minor was placed in secure detention; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-208(2)(b): secure care if the minor was committed to secure care.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-208(3): If the division has concerns regarding the minor's fitness to raise the minor's child, the division shall make a referral for services for the minor and the minor's child to the Division of Child and Family Services.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-301 Appropriation and funding of juvenile receiving centers.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Funding for juvenile receiving centers and youth services programs under this part is intended to be broad based, be provided by an appropriation by the Legislature to the division, and include federal grant money, local government money, and private donations.
