Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-304 Income and finances for minors in the custody of the division.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-304(1): If a minor is committed to the custody of the division, the division may establish:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-304(1)(a): an account for the minor that is administered by the division; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-304(1)(b): a joint account for the minor and the division at a federally insured financial institution.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-304(2): The division may:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-304(2)(a): collect funds earned or received by a minor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-304(2)(b): place the funds earned or received by the minor into an account described in Subsection (1).
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-304(3): The division may:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-304(3)(a): only use funds placed in an account described in Subsection (1) for the minor, including using the funds to pay restitution, reparations, fines, alimony, support payments, cost of care, or similar court-ordered payments owed by the minor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-304(3)(b): provide the minor with any funds remaining in an account described in Subsection (1) upon the minor's transition and termination from the custody of the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-304(4): In accordance with Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act, the division shall make rules to establish the administration of accounts and finances for minors in the custody of the division.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-401 Youth services for prevention and early intervention -- Program standards -- Program services.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-401(1): The division shall establish and operate prevention and early intervention youth services programs which shall include evidence-informed and research-informed interventions to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-401(1)(a): help youth and families avoid entry into the juvenile justice system; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-401(1)(b): improve attendance and academic achievement.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-401(2): The division shall adopt statewide policies and procedures, including minimum standards for the organization and operation of youth services programs.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-401(3): The division shall establish housing, programs, and procedures to ensure that minors who are receiving services under this section and who are not committed to the division are served separately from minors who are committed to the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-401(4): The division may enter into contracts with state and local governmental entities and private providers to provide the youth services.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-401(5): The division shall establish and administer juvenile receiving centers and other programs to provide temporary custody, care, risk-needs assessments, evaluations, and control for nonadjudicated and adjudicated minors placed with the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-401(6): The division shall prioritize use of evidence-based juvenile justice programs and practices.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-401(7): 80-6-703 Youth receiving services under this section or from the division may not be placed into the legal custody of the division unless the youth qualifies for such disposition under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-402 Community-based programs.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-402(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-402(1)(a): The division shall operate residential and nonresidential community-based  programs to provide care, treatment, and supervision for minors committed to the division by juvenile courts.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-402(1)(b): The division shall operate or contract for nonresidential community-based programs and independent living programs to provide care, treatment, and supervision of paroled juvenile offenders.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-402(2): The division shall adopt minimum standards for the organization and operation of community-based programs for minors.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-402(3): 80-6-703; 80-6-804 The division shall place minors committed to the division for community-based programs in the most appropriate program based upon the division's evaluation of the minor's needs and the division's available resources in accordance with Sections


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-403 Case management staff.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-403(1): The division shall provide a sufficient number of case management staff members to provide care, treatment, and supervision for juvenile offenders on parole and for minors committed to the division by the juvenile courts for community-based programs.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-403(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-403(2)(a): Case management staff shall develop treatment programs for each minor in the community, provide appropriate services, and monitor individual progress.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-403(2)(b): Progress reports shall be filed every three months with:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-403(2)(b)(i): the juvenile court for each minor committed to the division for community-based programs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-403(2)(b)(ii): the authority for each juvenile offender on parole.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-403(2)(c): The authority, in the case of juvenile offenders on parole, or the juvenile court, in the case of minors committed to the division for placement in community programs, shall be immediately notified, in writing, of any violation of law or of conditions of parole or placement.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-403(3): Case management staff shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-403(3)(a): conduct investigations and make reports requested by a juvenile court to aid the juvenile court in determining appropriate case dispositions; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-403(3)(b): conduct investigations and make reports requested by the authority to aid the authority in making appropriate dispositions in cases of parole, revocation, and termination.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-501 Detention facilities and services.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-501(1): The division shall provide detention facilities and services in each county, or group of counties, as the population demands, in accordance with this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-501(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-501(2)(a): The division is responsible for development, implementation, and administration of home detention services available in every judicial district.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-501(2)(b): The division shall establish criteria for placement in home detention.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-501(3): 80-5-202(1)(a) The division shall provide training regarding implementation of the rules made under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-502 New detention facilities.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-502(1): The division may issue requests for proposals to allow for the private construction of facilities suitable to meet the detention requirements of any county or group of counties, subject to approval by the governor.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-502(2): The governor shall furnish an analysis of the benefits of the proposals received to the Infrastructure and General Government Appropriations Subcommittee for the subcommittee's review.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-503 Secure care facilities.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-503(1): The division shall maintain and operate secure care facilities for the custody and rehabilitation of juvenile offenders:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-503(1)(a): who pose a danger of serious bodily harm to others;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-503(1)(b): who cannot be controlled in a less secure setting; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-503(1)(c): who have engaged in a pattern of conduct characterized by persistent and serious criminal offenses that, as demonstrated through the use of other alternatives, cannot be controlled in a less secure setting.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-503(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-503(2)(a): The director shall appoint an administrator for each secure care facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-503(2)(b): An administrator of a secure care facility shall have experience in social work, law, criminology, corrections, or a related field, and in administration.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-503(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-503(3)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-503(3)(a)(i): The division, in cooperation with the State Board of Education, shall provide instruction, or make instruction available, to juvenile offenders in secure care facilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-503(3)(a)(ii): The instruction shall be appropriate to the age, needs, and range of abilities of the juvenile offender.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-503(3)(b): A secure care facility shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-503(3)(b)(i): assess each juvenile offender to determine the juvenile offender's abilities, possible learning disabilities, interests, attitudes, and other attributes related to appropriate educational programs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-503(3)(b)(ii): provide prevocational education to juvenile offenders to acquaint juvenile offenders with vocations, and vocational requirements and opportunities.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-503(4): The division shall place juvenile offenders who have been committed to the division for secure care in a secure care facility, operated by the division or by a private entity, that is appropriate to ensure that humane care and rehabilitation opportunities are afforded to the juvenile offender.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-503(5): The division shall adopt standards, policies, and procedures for the regulation and operation of secure care facilities, consistent with state and federal law.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601 Harboring a runaway -- Reporting requirements -- Division of Child and Family Services to provide assistance -- Affirmative defense -- Providing shelter after notice.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(1): As used in this section, "harbor" means to provide shelter in:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(1)(a): the home of the person who is providing shelter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(1)(b): any structure over which the person providing the shelter has any control.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(2): (3); (2)(c) Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(2)(a): knowingly and intentionally harbors a child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(2)(b): knows at the time of harboring the child that the child is a runaway;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(2)(c): fails to notify one of the following, by telephone or other reasonable means, of the location of the child:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(2)(c)(i): the parent or guardian of the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(2)(c)(ii): the division; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(2)(c)(iii): a youth services center; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(2)(d): (2)(c) fails to notify a person described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(2)(d)(i): the time that the person becomes aware that the child is a runaway; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(2)(d)(ii): the time that the person begins harboring the child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(3): (2); (2); (2)(c); (d); 80-5-602 A person described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(3)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(3)(a)(i): a court order is issued authorizing a peace officer to take the child into custody; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(3)(a)(ii): the person notifies a peace officer, or the nearest detention facility, by telephone or other reasonable means, of the location of the child, within eight hours after the later of:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(3)(a)(ii)(A): the time that the person becomes aware that the child is a runaway; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(3)(a)(ii)(B): the time that the person begins harboring the child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(3)(b): 80-5-602
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(3)(b)(i): 80-5-602 the child is a runaway who consents to shelter, care, or licensed services under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(3)(b)(ii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(3)(b)(ii)(A): the person is unable to locate the child's parent or guardian; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(3)(b)(ii)(B): the child refuses to disclose the contact information for the child's parent or guardian.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(4): (2); 80-2-602 A person described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(4)(a): 80-2-602 if the person has an obligation under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(4)(b): if, within 48 hours after the person begins harboring the child:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(4)(b)(i): the person continues to harbor the child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(4)(b)(ii): the person does not make direct contact with:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(4)(b)(ii)(A): a parent or guardian of the child;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(4)(b)(ii)(B): the division;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(4)(b)(ii)(C): a youth services center; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(4)(b)(ii)(D): a peace officer or the nearest detention facility if a court order is issued authorizing a peace officer to take the child into custody.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(5): (2); (2); (3); (2); (3) It is an affirmative defense to the crime described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(5)(a): (2); (3) the person failed to provide notice as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(5)(b): (2); (3) the person provided the notice described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(6): Upon receipt of a report that a runaway is being harbored by a person:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(6)(a): a youth services center shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(6)(a)(i): notify the runaway's parent or guardian that a report has been made; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(6)(a)(ii): inform the runaway's parent or guardian of assistance available from the youth services center; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(6)(b): the division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(6)(b)(i): make a referral to the Division of Child and Family Services to determine whether the runaway is abused, neglected, or dependent; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(6)(b)(ii): if appropriate, make a referral for services for the runaway.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(7): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(7)(a): A parent or guardian of a runaway who is aware that the runaway is being harbored may notify a law enforcement agency and request assistance in retrieving the runaway.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(7)(b): The local law enforcement agency may assist the parent or guardian in retrieving the runaway.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(8): (2); (4) Nothing in this section prohibits a person from continuing to provide shelter to a runaway, after giving the notice described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(8)(a): a parent or guardian of the runaway consents to the continued provision of shelter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(8)(b): a peace officer or a parent or guardian of the runaway fails to retrieve the runaway.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(9): Nothing in this section prohibits a person from providing shelter to a child whose parent or guardian has intentionally:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(9)(a): ceased to maintain physical custody of the child; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(9)(b): failed to make reasonable arrangements for the safety, care, and physical custody of the child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(10): Nothing in this section prohibits:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(10)(a): a juvenile receiving center or a youth services center from providing shelter to a runaway in accordance with the requirements of this chapter and the rules relating to a juvenile receiving center or a youth services center; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-601(10)(b): a government agency from taking custody of a child as otherwise provided by law.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602 Homeless youth -- Consent to shelter, care, or services by a homeless youth.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(1)(a): "Care" means providing:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(1)(a)(i): assistance to obtain food, clothing, hygiene products, or other basic necessities;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(1)(a)(ii): access to a bed, showering facility, or transportation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(1)(a)(iii): assistance with school enrollment or attendance.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(1)(b): "Licensed services" means a service provided by a temporary homeless youth shelter, a youth services center, or other facility that is licensed to provide the service to a homeless youth.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(1)(c): "Service" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(1)(c)(i): youth services;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(1)(c)(ii): child welfare or juvenile court case management or advocacy;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(1)(c)(iii): aftercare services; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(1)(c)(iv): independent living skills training.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(2): A homeless youth may consent to temporary shelter, care, or licensed services if the homeless youth:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(2)(a): is at least 15 years old; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(2)(b): manages the homeless youth's own financial affairs, regardless of the source of income.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(3): (2) In determining consent under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(4): (2); 80-5-601(4) A person who provides shelter, care, or licensed services to a homeless youth who consents to the shelter, care, or licensed services under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(4)(a): 80-5-601(4) shall report to the division as required under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-602(4)(b): may provide the homeless youth a referral to temporary or permanent housing, employment resources, medical or dental providers, or counseling.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-701 Youth Parole Authority -- Creation -- Members.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-701(1): There is created the Youth Parole Authority within the division.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-701(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-701(2)(a): The authority is composed of 10 part-time members and five pro tempore members who are residents of this state.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-701(2)(b): No more than three pro tempore members may serve on the authority at any one time.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-702 Member qualifications -- Expenses.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-702(1): As used in this section, "member" means both a part-time member and a pro tempore member of the authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-702(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-702(2)(a): Except as required by Subsection (2)(b), the governor, with the advice and consent of the Senate, shall appoint or reappoint members to four-year terms.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-702(2)(b): The governor shall, at the time of appointment or reappointment, adjust the length of terms to ensure that the terms of members are staggered so that approximately half of the authority is appointed every two years.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-702(3): A member shall have training or experience in social work, law, juvenile or criminal justice, or related behavioral sciences.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-702(4): When a vacancy occurs in the membership for any reason, the governor shall, with the advice and consent of the Senate, appoint a replacement for the unexpired term.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-702(5): During the tenure of the member's appointment, a member may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-702(5)(a): be an employee of the department, other than in the member's capacity as a member of the authority;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-702(5)(b): hold any public office;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-702(5)(c): hold any position in the state's juvenile justice system; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-702(5)(d): be an employee, officer, advisor, policy board member, or subcontractor of any juvenile justice agency or the juvenile justice agency's contractor.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-702(6): In extraordinary circumstances or when a regular member is absent or otherwise unavailable, the chair may assign a pro tempore member to act in the absent member's place.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-702(7): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-702(7)(a): 63A-3-106 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-702(7)(b): 63A-3-107 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-702(7)(c): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 rules made by the Division of Finance in accordance with Sections


Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703 Authority responsibilities -- Administrative officer of the authority.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(1): The authority is responsible for:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(1)(a): the release of a juvenile offender from secure care; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(1)(b): the rescission, revocation, and termination of parole for a juvenile offender.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(2): Chapter 6, Part 8, Commitment and Parole In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(2)(a): determine when and under what conditions a juvenile offender in secure care is eligible for parole;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(2)(b): establish policies and procedures regarding:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(2)(b)(i): the authority's governance, meetings, and hearings;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(2)(b)(ii): the conduct of proceedings before the authority;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(2)(b)(iii): the parole of a juvenile offender; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(2)(b)(iv): for which parole for a juvenile offender may be granted, rescinded, revoked, modified, and terminated; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(2)(c): determine appropriate parole dates for juvenile offenders.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(3): The division's case management staff shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(3)(a): implement plans for parole; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(3)(b): supervise a juvenile offender on parole.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(4): The division shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(4)(a): permit the authority to have reasonable access to a juvenile offender in secure care; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(4)(b): furnish all pertinent data requested by the authority in matters of parole, revocation, and termination.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(5): The director shall appoint an administrative officer of the authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(6): The administrative officer is responsible for the day-to-day operations of the authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(7): The authority and the administrative officer have power to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(7)(a): issue subpoenas;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(7)(b): compel attendance of witnesses;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(7)(c): compel production of books, papers, and other documents; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(7)(d): administer oaths and take testimony under oath for the purposes of conducting the hearings.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-5-703(8): The administrative officer shall maintain summary records of all hearings and provide written notice to the juvenile offender of a decision and the reason for the decision.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(1): "Aftercare services" means the same as the term "aftercare" is defined in 45 C.F.R. 1351.1.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(2): 80-5-701 "Authority" means the Youth Parole Authority created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(3): 63M-7-201 "Commission" means the State Commission on Criminal and Juvenile Justice created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(4): "Compensatory service" means service or unpaid work performed by a minor in lieu of the payment of a fine, fee, or restitution.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(5): 80-5-102 "Control" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(6): 80-6-207 "Detention hearing" means a proceeding under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(7): 80-5-202 "Detention guidelines" means standards, established by the division in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(8): "Discharge" means a written order of the authority that removes a juvenile offender from the authority's jurisdiction.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(9): 80-5-103 "Division" means the Division of Juvenile Justice and Youth Services created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(10): "Family-based setting" means a home that is licensed to allow a minor to reside at the home, including a foster home, proctor care, or residential care by a professional parent.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(11): "Formal referral" means a written report from a peace officer, or other person, informing the juvenile court that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(11)(a): an offense committed by a minor is, or appears to be, within the juvenile court's jurisdiction; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(11)(b): the minor's case must be reviewed by a juvenile probation officer or a prosecuting attorney.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(12): 53G-8-211 "Habitual truant" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(13): "Material loss" means an uninsured:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(13)(a): property loss;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(13)(b): out-of-pocket monetary loss for property that is stolen, damaged, or destroyed;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(13)(c): lost wages because of an injury, time spent as a witness, or time spent assisting the police or prosecution; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(13)(d): medical expense.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(14): 53G-8-211; 80-6-302 "Referral" means a formal referral, a referral to the juvenile court under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(15): "Rescission" means a written order of the authority that rescinds a date for parole.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(16): "Restitution" means money or services that the juvenile court, or a juvenile probation officer if the minor agrees to a nonjudicial adjustment, orders a minor to pay or render to a victim for the minor's wrongful act or conduct.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(17): 80-6-806 "Revocation" means a written order of the authority that, after a hearing and determination under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(17)(a): terminates supervision of a juvenile offender's parole; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(17)(b): directs a juvenile offender to return to secure care.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(18): 80-6-701 "Temporary custody" means the control and responsibility of a minor, before an adjudication under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(19): "Termination" means a written order of the authority that terminates a juvenile offender from parole.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(20): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(20)(a): "Victim" means a person that the juvenile court determines suffered a material loss as a result of a minor's wrongful act or conduct.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(20)(b): "Victim" includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(20)(b)(i): any person directly harmed by the minor's wrongful act or conduct in the course of the scheme, conspiracy, or pattern if the minor's wrongful act or conduct is an offense that involves an element of a scheme, a conspiracy, or a pattern of criminal activity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-102(20)(b)(ii): the Utah Office for Victims of Crime.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-201 Minor taken into temporary custody by peace officer, private citizen, or probation officer -- Grounds -- Protective custody.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-201(1): 80-6-202; 53G-6-208; 53G-8-211 A minor may be taken into temporary  custody by a peace officer without a court order, or a warrant under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-201(1)(a): the minor has committed an offense under municipal, state, or federal law;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-201(1)(b): the minor seriously endangers the minor's own welfare or the welfare of others and taking the minor into temporary custody appears to be necessary for the protection of the minor or others;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-201(1)(c): the minor has run away or escaped from the minor's parents, guardian, or custodian; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-201(1)(d): 53G-6-208; 53G-8-211 the minor is:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-201(1)(d)(i): subject to the state's compulsory education law; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-201(1)(d)(ii): 53G-6-208; 53G-8-211 subject to Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-201(2): 77-7-3 A private citizen may take a minor into temporary  custody if under the circumstances the private citizen could make a citizen's arrest under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-201(3): A juvenile probation officer may take a minor into temporary custody:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-201(3)(a): under the same circumstances as a peace officer in Subsection (1); or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-201(3)(b): if the juvenile probation officer has a reasonable suspicion that  the minor has violated the conditions of the minor's probation.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-201(4): 80-2a-202; 80-3-204
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-201(4)(a): 80-2a-202; 80-3-204 Nothing in this part shall be construed to prevent a peace officer or the Division of Child and Family Services from taking a minor into protective custody under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-201(4)(b): If a peace officer or the Division of Child and Family Services takes a minor into protective custody, the provisions of Chapter 2, Child Welfare Services, Chapter 2a, Removal and Protective Custody of a Child, and Chapter 3, Abuse, Neglect, and Dependency Proceedings shall govern.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202 Warrants for minors.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(1): 80-6-305; 80-6-503; 78A-6-351
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(1)(a): 80-6-305; 80-6-503; 78A-6-351 Except as otherwise provided in this section, after a petition is filed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(1)(a)(i): 78A-6-351 there is probable cause to believe that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(1)(a)(i)(A): the minor has committed an offense that would be a felony if committed by an adult;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(1)(a)(i)(B): 78A-6-351 the minor has failed to appear after the minor or the minor's parent, guardian, or custodian has been legally served with a summons in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(1)(a)(i)(C): there is a substantial likelihood the minor will not respond to a summons;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(1)(a)(i)(D): a summons cannot be served and the minor's present whereabouts are unknown;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(1)(a)(i)(E): serving a summons for the minor will be ineffectual;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(1)(a)(i)(F): the minor seriously endangers others or the public and temporary custody appears to be necessary for the protection of others or the public; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(1)(a)(i)(G): the minor is a runaway or has escaped from the minor's parent, guardian, or custodian; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(1)(a)(ii): the minor is under the continuing jurisdiction of the juvenile court and there is probable cause to believe that the minor:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(1)(a)(ii)(A): has left the custody of the person or agency vested by a court with legal custody, or guardianship of the minor, without permission; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(1)(a)(ii)(B): has violated a court order.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(1)(b): A warrant issued under this Subsection (1) shall be:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(1)(b)(i): filed in accordance with Utah Rules of Juvenile Procedure, Rule 7; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(1)(b)(ii): executed in accordance with Title 77, Chapter 7, Arrest, by Whom, and How Made.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(2): A juvenile court may not issue a warrant for a minor to be taken into temporary custody for:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(2)(a): a status offense;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(2)(b): an infraction; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(2)(c): being a habitual truant.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(3)(a): For a minor not eligible for a warrant under Subsection (2), a juvenile court may issue a warrant that directs a minor to be returned home, to the juvenile court, or to a shelter or other nonsecure facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(3)(b): A warrant under Subsection (3)(a) may not direct a minor to secure care or secure detention.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-202(4): Subsection (2) does not apply to a minor who is under Chapter 6, Part 11, Interstate Compact for Juveniles.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205 Admission to detention -- Alternative to detention -- Rights of a minor in detention.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(1): 80-6-203 If a minor is taken to a detention facility under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(1)(a): admit the minor to secure detention;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(1)(b): admit the minor to home detention;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(1)(c): place the minor in an alternative to detention, except that the staff member may not place the minor in a correctional facility that is intended to hold adults accused or convicted of offenses as an alternative to detention; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(1)(d): if the minor is a child, return the minor home upon a written promise by the minor's parent, guardian, or custodian to bring the minor to the juvenile court at a time set or without restriction.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(2): 80-6-202; 80-6-806 The designated staff member may not admit a minor to detention under Subsection (1) unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(2)(a): the minor is detainable based on the detention guidelines; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(2)(b): 80-6-202; 80-6-806 the minor has been brought to detention in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(2)(b)(i): a court order;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(2)(b)(ii): 80-6-202 a warrant described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(2)(b)(iii): 80-6-806 a division warrant described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(3): If the designated staff member determines to admit a minor to home detention, the staff member shall notify the juvenile court of that determination.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(4): Even if a minor is eligible for secure detention, a peace officer or other person who takes a minor to a detention facility, or the designated staff member of the detention facility, may release a minor to a less restrictive alternative than secure detention.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(5)(a): If a minor taken to a detention facility does not qualify for admission under detention guidelines or this section, a designated staff member of the detention facility shall arrange an appropriate alternative, including admitting a minor to a juvenile receiving center or a shelter facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(5)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(5)(b)(i): Except as otherwise provided by this section, a minor may not be placed or kept in secure detention while court proceedings are pending.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(5)(b)(ii): A child may not be placed or kept in a shelter facility while court proceedings are pending, unless the child is in protective custody in accordance with Chapter 3, Abuse, Neglect, and Dependency Proceedings.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(6): If a minor is taken into temporary custody and admitted to a secure detention, or another alternative to detention, a designated staff member of the detention facility shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(6)(a): immediately notify the minor's parent, guardian, or custodian; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(6)(b): promptly notify the juvenile court of the placement.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(7): If a minor is admitted to secure detention, or another alternative to detention, outside the county of the minor's residence and a juvenile court determines, in a detention hearing, that secure detention, or an alternative to detention, of the minor shall continue, the juvenile court shall direct the sheriff of the county of the minor's residence to transport the minor to secure detention or another alternative to detention in that county.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(8): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(8)(a): Subject to Subsection (8)(b), a minor admitted to detention has a right to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(8)(a)(i): phone the minor's parent, guardian, or attorney immediately after the minor is admitted to detention; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(8)(a)(ii): confer in private, at any time, with an attorney, cleric, parent, guardian, or custodian.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(8)(b): The division may:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(8)(b)(i): establish a schedule for which a minor in detention may visit or phone a person described in Subsection (8)(a);
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(8)(b)(ii): allow a minor in detention to visit or call persons described in Subsection (8)(a) in special circumstances;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(8)(b)(iii): limit the number and length of calls and visits for a minor in detention to persons described in Subsection (8)(a) on account of scheduling, facility, or personnel constraints; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(8)(b)(iv): limit the minor's rights described in Subsection (8)(a) if a compelling reason exists to limit the minor's rights.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-205(8)(c): A minor admitted to detention shall be immediately advised of the minor's rights described in this Subsection (8).


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206 Interrogation of a child -- Presence of a parent, legal guardian, or other adult --  Prohibition on false information or unauthorized statement -- Admissibility of admission, confession, or statement by child.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(1): As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(1)(a): "Custodial interrogation" means any interrogation of a child while the individual is in custody.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(1)(b)(i): "Friendly adult" means an adult:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(1)(b)(i)(A): who has an established relationship with the child to the extent that the adult can provide meaningful advice and concerned help to the child should the need arise; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(1)(b)(i)(B): who is not hostile or adverse to the child's interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(1)(b)(ii): "Friendly adult" does not include a parent or guardian of the child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(1)(c): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(1)(c)(i): "Interrogation" means any express questioning or any words or actions that are reasonably likely to elicit an incriminating response.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(1)(c)(ii): "Interrogation" does not include words or actions normally attendant to arrest and custody.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(2)(a): If a child is subject to a custodial interrogation for an offense, the child has the right to have:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(2)(a)(i): the child's parent or guardian present during an interrogation of the child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(2)(a)(ii): a friendly adult present during an interrogation of the child if:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(2)(a)(ii)(A): there is reason to believe that the child's parent or guardian has abused or threatened the child; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(2)(a)(ii)(B): the child's parent's or guardian's interest is adverse to the child's interest, including that the parent or guardian is a victim or a codefendant of the offense alleged to have been committed by the child.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(2)(b): A child's parent or guardian, or a friendly adult, is present at a custodial interrogation if:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(2)(b)(i): the parent, guardian, or friendly adult attends the custodial interrogation in person or by video; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(2)(b)(ii): an interpreter is provided to the child and the parent, guardian, or friendly adult if the child or the parent, guardian, or friendly adult is unable to speak or understand English.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(3): 80-2-705 If a child is subject to a custodial interrogation for an offense, the child may not be interrogated unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(3)(a): the child has been advised, in accordance with Subsection (4), of:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(3)(a)(i): the child's constitutional rights; and

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(4)(l): Do you want to talk to me?

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(10)(a): If a peace officer or juvenile probation officer intentionally, knowingly, or recklessly fails to comply with the requirements for a custodial interrogation of a child as described in this section, any admission, confession, or statement made by the child as a result of the custodial interrogation is presumed:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(10)(a)(i): to not be voluntarily, knowingly, and intelligently made; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(10)(a)(ii): to not be admissible as evidence against the child.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-206(10)(b)(ii): if the child has a right to have a parent, guardian, or friendly adult present under this section, the child's right to have a parent or guardian, or a friendly adult, present during the custodial interrogation.

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-303.5(1): If the juvenile court receives a referral for an offense committed by a minor that is, or appears to be, within the juvenile court's jurisdiction, or for the minor being a habitual truant, a juvenile probation officer shall make a preliminary inquiry in accordance with this section to determine whether the minor is eligible to enter into a nonjudicial adjustment.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-303.5(2): If a minor is referred to the juvenile court for multiple offenses arising from a single criminal episode, and the minor is eligible under this section for a nonjudicial adjustment, the juvenile probation officer shall offer the minor one nonjudicial adjustment for all offenses arising from the single criminal episode.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-303.5(4)(a): the minor:

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-304 Nonjudicial adjustments.
-------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-304(1): (4) For a nonjudicial adjustment, the juvenile probation officer may require a minor to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-304(1)(a): (4) pay a financial penalty of no more than $250 to the juvenile court, subject to the terms established under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-304(1)(b): pay restitution to any victim;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-304(1)(c): complete community or compensatory service;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-304(1)(d): attend counseling or treatment with an appropriate provider;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-304(1)(e): attend substance abuse treatment or counseling;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-304(1)(f): comply with specified restrictions on activities or associations;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-304(1)(g): attend victim-offender mediation if requested by the victim; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-304(1)(h): comply with any other reasonable action that is in the interest of the minor, the community, or the victim.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-304(2): 80-6-303.5
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-304(2)(a): 80-6-303.5 Within seven days of receiving a referral that appears to be eligible for a nonjudicial adjustment in accordance with Section

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-304(2)(b)(ii): documentation and evidence of compensation or reimbursement from an insurance company or an agency of the state, any other state, or the federal government received as a direct result of the crime for injury, loss of earnings, or out-of-pocket loss; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-304(2)(b)(iii): proof of identification, including home and work address and telephone numbers.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-304(2)(c): The inability, failure, or refusal of the victim to provide all or part of the requested information shall result in the juvenile probation officer determining restitution based on the best information available.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-304(3): The juvenile probation officer may not predicate acceptance of an offer of a nonjudicial adjustment on an admission of guilt.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-307(2): 63M-7-401.1 When preparing a dispositional report and recommendation in a minor's case, the juvenile probation officer,  or other agency designated by the juvenile court, shall consider the juvenile disposition guidelines, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-307(3): 80-6-305 Where the allegations of a petition filed under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401 Definitions -- Competency to proceed.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(1): 77-15-2 As used in this part:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(1)(a): "Competency" or "competent to proceed" means that a minor has:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(1)(a)(i): a present ability to consult with counsel with a reasonable degree of rational understanding; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(1)(a)(ii): a rational as well as factual understanding of the proceedings.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(1)(b): "Competency evaluation" means an evaluation conducted by a forensic evaluator to determine if a minor is competent to stand for trial or adjudication for pending charges.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(1)(c): 77-15-2 "Forensic evaluator" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(1)(d): "Not competent to proceed" means an individual is not competent to stand for trial or adjudication for pending charges.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(2): 80-6-305; 80-6-503 If a petition is filed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(3): The written motion shall contain:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(3)(a): a certificate that it is filed in good faith and on reasonable grounds to believe the minor is not competent to proceed due to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(3)(a)(i): a mental illness;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(3)(a)(ii): an intellectual disability or a related condition; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(3)(a)(iii): developmental immaturity;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(3)(b): a recital of the facts, observations, and conversations with the minor that have formed the basis for the motion; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(3)(c): if filed by defense counsel, the motion shall contain information that can be revealed without invading the lawyer-client privilege.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(4): The motion may be:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(4)(a): based upon knowledge or information and belief; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(4)(b): filed by:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(4)(b)(i): the minor alleged not competent to proceed;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(4)(b)(ii): any person acting on the minor's behalf;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(4)(b)(iii): the prosecuting attorney;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(4)(b)(iv): the attorney  guardian ad litem; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(4)(b)(v): any person having custody or supervision over the minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(5)(a): The juvenile court  may raise the issue of a minor's competency at any time.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(5)(b): If raised by the juvenile  court, counsel for each party shall be permitted to address the issue of competency.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-401(5)(c): The juvenile court shall state the basis for the finding that there are reasonable grounds to believe the minor is not competent to proceed.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402 Procedure -- Standard.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(1): 80-6-401 When a written motion is filed in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(2)(a): If a motion for inquiry is opposed by either party, the juvenile  court shall, before granting or denying the motion, hold a limited hearing solely for the purpose of determining the sufficiency of the motion.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(2)(b): If the juvenile  court finds that the allegations of incompetency raise a bona fide doubt as to the minor's competency to proceed, the juvenile court  shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(2)(b)(i): enter an order for an evaluation of the minor's competency to proceed; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(2)(b)(ii): set a date for a hearing on the issue of the minor's competency.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(3): After the granting of a motion, and before a full competency hearing, the juvenile  court may order the department to evaluate the minor and to report to the juvenile  court concerning the minor's mental condition.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(4): The minor shall be evaluated by a forensic evaluator who:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(4)(a): has experience in juvenile forensic evaluations and juvenile brain development;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(4)(b): if it becomes apparent that the minor is not competent due to an intellectual disability or related condition, has experience in intellectual disability or related conditions; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(4)(c): is not involved in the current treatment of the minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(5): The petitioner or other party, as directed by the juvenile court, shall provide all information and materials relevant to a determination of the minor's competency to the department within seven days of the juvenile court's order, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(5)(a): the motion;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(5)(b): the arrest or incident reports pertaining to the charged offense;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(5)(c): the minor's known delinquency history information;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(5)(d): the minor's probation record relevant to competency;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(5)(e): known prior mental health evaluations and treatments; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(5)(f): consistent with 20 U.S.C. Sec. 1232g (b)(1)(E)(ii)(I), records pertaining to the minor's education.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(6)(a): The minor's parent or guardian, the prosecuting attorney, the defense attorney, and the attorney guardian ad litem, shall cooperate, by executing releases of information when necessary, in providing the relevant information and materials to the forensic evaluator, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(6)(a)(i): medical records;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(6)(a)(ii): prior mental evaluations; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(6)(a)(iii): records of diagnosis or treatment of substance abuse disorders.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(6)(b): The minor shall cooperate, by executing a release of information when necessary, in providing the relevant information and materials to the forensic evaluator regarding records of diagnosis or treatment of a substance abuse disorder.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(7): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(7)(a): In conducting the evaluation and in the report determining if a minor is competent to proceed, the forensic evaluator shall inform the juvenile court of the forensic evaluator's opinion whether:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(7)(a)(i): the minor has a present ability to consult with counsel with a reasonable degree of rational understanding; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(7)(a)(ii): the minor has a rational as well as factual understanding of the proceedings.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(7)(b): In evaluating the minor, the forensic evaluator shall consider the minor's present ability to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(7)(b)(i): understand the charges or allegations against the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(7)(b)(ii): communicate facts, events, and states of mind;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(7)(b)(iii): understand the range of possible penalties associated with the allegations against the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(7)(b)(iv): engage in reasoned choice of legal strategies and options;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(7)(b)(v): understand the adversarial nature of the proceedings against the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(7)(b)(vi): manifest behavior sufficient to allow the juvenile court to proceed;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(7)(b)(vii): testify relevantly; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(7)(b)(viii): any other factor determined to be relevant to the forensic evaluator.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(8): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(8)(a): The forensic evaluator shall provide an initial report to the juvenile court, the prosecuting and defense attorneys, and the attorney guardian ad litem, if applicable, within 30 days of the receipt of the juvenile court's order.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(8)(b): If the forensic evaluator informs the juvenile court that additional time is needed, the juvenile court may grant, taking into consideration the custody status of the minor, up to an additional 15 days to provide the report to the juvenile court and counsel.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(8)(c): The forensic evaluator must provide the report within 45 days from the receipt of the juvenile court's order unless, for good cause shown, the juvenile court authorizes an additional period of time to complete the evaluation and provide the report.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(8)(d): The report shall inform the juvenile court of the forensic evaluator's opinion concerning the minor's competency.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(9): If the forensic evaluator's opinion is that the minor is not competent to proceed, the report shall indicate:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(9)(a): the nature of the minor's:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(9)(a)(i): mental illness;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(9)(a)(ii): intellectual disability or related condition; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(9)(a)(iii): developmental immaturity;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(9)(b): the relationship of the minor's mental illness, intellectual disability, related condition, or developmental immaturity to the minor's incompetence;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(9)(c): whether there is a substantial likelihood that the minor may attain competency in the foreseeable future;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(9)(d): the amount of time estimated for the minor to achieve competency if the minor undergoes competency attainment treatment, including medication;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(9)(e): the sources of information used by the forensic evaluator; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(9)(f): the basis for clinical findings and opinions.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(10): Regardless of whether a minor consents to a competency evaluation, any statement made by the minor in the course of the competency evaluation, any testimony by the forensic evaluator based upon any statement made by the minor in the competency evaluation, and any other fruits of the statement made by the minor in the competency evaluation:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(10)(a): may not be admitted in evidence against the minor in a proceeding under this chapter, except the statement may be admitted on an issue respecting the mental condition on which the minor has introduced evidence; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(10)(b): may be admitted where relevant to a determination of the minor's competency.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(12): When the report is received, the juvenile court shall set a date for a competency hearing that shall be held in not less than five and not more than 15 days, unless the juvenile court enlarges the time for good cause.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(13): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(13)(a): A minor shall be presumed competent unless the juvenile court, by a preponderance of the evidence, finds the minor not competent to proceed.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-402(13)(b): The burden of proof is upon the proponent of incompetency to proceed.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403 Disposition on finding of not competent to proceed -- Subsequent hearings -- Notice to prosecuting attorneys.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(1): If the juvenile court determines that the minor is not competent to proceed, and there is a substantial likelihood that the minor may attain competency in the foreseeable future, the juvenile court shall notify the department of the finding and allow the department 30 days to develop an attainment plan for the minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(2): The attainment plan shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(2)(a): any services or treatment the minor has been or is currently receiving that are necessary to attain competency;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(2)(b): any additional services or treatment the minor may require to attain competency;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(2)(c): an assessment of the parent, custodian, or guardian's ability to access or provide any recommended treatment or services;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(2)(d): any special conditions or supervision that may be necessary for the safety of the minor or others during the attainment period; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(2)(e): the likelihood that the minor will attain competency and the amount of time likely required for the minor to attain competency.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(3): The department shall provide the attainment plan to the juvenile court, the prosecuting attorney, the defense attorney, and the attorney guardian ad litem at least three days before the competency disposition hearing.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(4)(a): During the attainment period, the minor shall remain in the least restrictive appropriate setting.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(4)(b): A finding of not competent to proceed does not grant authority for a juvenile court to place a minor in the custody of a division of the department, or create eligibility for services from the Division of Services for People With Disabilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(4)(c): If the juvenile court orders the minor to be held in detention during the attainment period, the juvenile court shall make the following findings on the record:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(4)(c)(i): the placement is the least restrictive appropriate setting;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(4)(c)(ii): the placement is in the best interest of the minor;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(4)(c)(iii): the minor will have access to the services and treatment required by the attainment plan in the placement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(4)(c)(iv): the placement is necessary for the safety of the minor or others.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(4)(d): A juvenile court shall terminate an order of detention related to the pending proceeding for a minor who is not competent to proceed in that matter if:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(4)(d)(i): the most severe allegation against the minor if committed by an adult is a class B misdemeanor;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(4)(d)(ii): more than 60 days have passed after the day on which the juvenile court adjudicated the minor not competent to proceed; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(4)(d)(iii): the minor has not attained competency.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(5): (5)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(5)(a): At any time that the minor becomes competent to proceed during the attainment period, the department shall notify the juvenile court, the prosecuting attorney, the defense attorney, and the attorney guardian ad litem.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(5)(b): (5)(a) The juvenile court shall hold a hearing with 15 business days of notice from the department described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(6): Title 26B, Chapter 6, Part 6, Admission to an Intermediate Care Facility for People with an Intellectual Disability; Title 26B, Chapter 5, Part 3, Utah State Hospital and Other Mental Health Facilities; Title 26B, Chapter 5, Part 4, Commitment of Persons Under Age 18; (6)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(6)(a): Title 26B, Chapter 6, Part 6, Admission to an Intermediate Care Facility for People with an Intellectual Disability; Title 26B, Chapter 5, Part 3, Utah State Hospital and Other Mental Health Facilities; Title 26B, Chapter 5, Part 4, Commitment of Persons Under Age 18 If at any time during the attainment period the juvenile court finds that there is not a substantial probability that the minor will attain competency in the foreseeable future, the juvenile court shall terminate the competency proceeding, dismiss the petition or information without prejudice, and release the minor from any custody order related to the pending proceeding, unless the prosecuting attorney or any other individual informs the juvenile court that commitment proceedings will be initiated in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(6)(a)(i): Title 26B, Chapter 6, Part 6, Admission to an Intermediate Care Facility for People with an Intellectual Disability
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(6)(a)(ii): Title 26B, Chapter 5, Part 3, Utah State Hospital and Other Mental Health Facilities if the minor is 18 years old or older,
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(6)(a)(iii): Title 26B, Chapter 5, Part 4, Commitment of Persons Under Age 18 if the minor is a child,
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(6)(b): (6)(a) The prosecuting attorney shall initiate the proceedings described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(7): During the attainment period, the juvenile court may order a hearing or rehearing at anytime on the juvenile court's own motion or upon recommendation of any interested party or the department.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(8): (8)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(8)(a): Within three months of the juvenile court's approval of the attainment plan, the department shall provide a report on the minor's progress towards competence.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(8)(b): (8)(a) The report described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(8)(b)(i): compliance with the attainment plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(8)(b)(ii): progress towards competency based on the issues identified in the original competency evaluation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(8)(b)(iii): current mental illness, intellectual disability or related condition, or developmental immaturity, and need for treatment, if any, and whether there is substantial likelihood of the minor attaining competency within six months.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(9): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(9)(a): Within 30 days of receipt of the report, the juvenile court shall hold a hearing to determine the minor's current status.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(9)(b): At the hearing, the burden of proving the minor is competent is on the proponent of competency.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(9)(c): The juvenile court shall determine by a preponderance of the evidence whether the minor is competent to proceed.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(10): If the minor has not attained competency after the initial three month attainment period but is showing reasonable progress towards attainment of competency, the juvenile court may extend the attainment period up to an additional three months.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(11): The department shall provide an updated juvenile competency evaluation at the conclusion of the six month attainment period to advise the juvenile court on the minor's current competency status.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(12): If the minor does not attain competency within six months after the juvenile court initially finds the minor not competent to proceed, the court shall terminate the competency proceedings and dismiss the petition or information filed without prejudice, unless good cause is shown that there is a substantial likelihood the minor will attain competency within one year from the initial finding of not competent to proceed.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(13): In the event a minor has an unauthorized leave lasting more than 24 hours, the attainment period shall toll until the minor returns.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(14): (14)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(14)(a): Regardless of whether a minor consents to attainment, any statement made by the minor in the course of attainment, any testimony by the forensic evaluator based upon any statement made by the minor in the course of attainment, and any other fruits of a statement made by the minor in the course of attainment:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(14)(a)(i): may not be admitted in evidence against the minor in a proceeding under this chapter, except the statement may be admitted on an issue respecting the mental condition on which the minor has introduced evidence; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(14)(a)(ii): may be admitted where relevant to a determination of the minor's competency.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-403(14)(b): (14)(a) Before evaluating the minor during the attainment period, a forensic evaluator shall specifically advise the minor, and the minor's parent or guardian if reasonably available, of the limits of confidentiality provided in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-501 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-501(1): 80-6-502; 80-6-503 "Minor" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-501(1)(a): an individual:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-501(1)(a)(i): who is at least 18 years old and younger than 25 years old; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-501(1)(a)(ii): whose case is under the jurisdiction of the juvenile court; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-501(1)(b): 80-6-502; 80-6-503 an individual:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-501(1)(b)(i): who is younger than 21 years old;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-501(1)(b)(ii): 80-6-502; 80-6-503 who is charged with, or convicted of, an offense under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-501(1)(b)(iii): whose case is under the jurisdiction of the district court.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-501(2): 80-6-503 "Qualifying offense" means an offense described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-501(3): "Separate offense" means any offense that is not a qualifying offense.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-505 Criminal proceedings for a minor bound over to district court.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-505(1): 80-6-504; 76-3-206(2)(b); 76-3-206(2)(b); 76-3-207.5(3); 76-3-209 If the juvenile court binds a minor over to the district court in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-505(1)(a): 76-3-206(2)(b) the minor is not subject to a sentence of death in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-505(1)(b): 76-3-206(2)(b); 76-3-207.5(3); 76-3-209 the minor is not subject to a sentence of life without parole in accordance with Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-505(2): A minor who is bound over to the district court to answer as an adult is not entitled to a preliminary hearing in the district court.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-505(3): If a minor is bound over to the district court and detained in a detention facility, the district court may order the minor be detained in another place of confinement that is considered appropriate by the district court, including a jail or other place of pretrial confinement for adults if the minor's conduct or condition endangers the safety and welfare of others in the detention facility.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-507 Commitment of a minor by a district court.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-507(1): (1); (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-507(1)(a): If the district court determines that probation is not appropriate and commitment to prison is an appropriate sentence when sentencing a minor:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-507(1)(a)(i): the district court shall order the minor committed to prison; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-507(1)(a)(ii): the minor shall be provisionally housed in a secure care facility  until the minor reaches 25 years old, unless released earlier from incarceration by the Board of Pardons and Parole.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-507(1)(b): (1); (1)(a) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-507(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (1); (2)(a)

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-507(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-507(3)(a): When a minor is committed to prison but provisionally housed in a secure care facility  under this section, the district court and the division shall immediately notify the Board of Pardons and Parole so that the minor may be scheduled for a hearing according to board procedures.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-507(3)(b): If a minor who is provisionally housed in a secure care facility  under this section has not been paroled or otherwise released from incarceration by the time the minor reaches 25 years old, the division shall as soon as reasonably possible, but not later than when the minor reaches 25 years and 6 months old, transfer the minor to the physical custody of the Department of Corrections.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-507(4): Upon the commitment of a minor to the custody of the division or the Department of Corrections under this section, the Board of Pardons and Parole has authority over the minor for purposes of parole, pardon, commutation, termination of sentence, remission of fines or forfeitures, orders of restitution, and all other purposes authorized by law.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-507(5): The authority  shall:

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-507(5)(b): forward to the Board of Pardons and Parole any information or recommendations concerning the minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-507(6): Commitment of a minor under this section is a prison commitment for all sentencing purposes.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-508 Blended plea -- Not permitted.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-508(1): 76-1-401 As used in this section:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-508(1)(a): "Blended plea" means a plea bargain entered into by a minor that results in a combination of a juvenile adjudication and disposition and a criminal conviction and sentence for a criminal offense that arises from a single criminal episode.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-508(1)(b): 76-1-401 "Single criminal episode" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-508(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-508(2)(a): Beginning May 1, 2024, a district court, juvenile court, or a justice court may not accept a plea bargain that is a blended plea.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-508(2)(b): Any criminal conviction or sentence resulting from a blended plea that is entered into on or after May 1, 2024, is void.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-608 When photographs, fingerprints, or HIV infection tests may be taken -- Distribution -- DNA collection -- Reimbursement.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-608(1): The division  shall take a photograph and fingerprints of a minor who is:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-608(1)(a): 14 years old or older at the time of the alleged commission of an offense that would be a felony if the minor were 18 years old or older; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-608(1)(b): admitted to a detention facility for the alleged commission of the offense.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-608(2): The juvenile court  shall order a minor who is 14 years old or older at the time that the minor is alleged to have committed an offense described in Subsection (2)(a) or (b)  to have the minor's fingerprints taken at a detention facility or a local law enforcement agency if the minor is:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-608(2)(a): adjudicated for an offense that would be a class A misdemeanor if the minor were 18 years old or older; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-608(2)(b): adjudicated for an offense that would be a felony if the minor were 18 years old or older and the minor was not admitted to a detention facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-608(3): The juvenile court  shall take a photograph of a minor who is:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-608(3)(a): 14 years old or older at the time the minor was alleged to have committed an offense that would be a felony or a class A misdemeanor if the minor were 18 years old or older; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-608(3)(b): adjudicated for the offense described in Subsection (3)(a).
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-608(4): If a minor's fingerprints are taken under this section, the minor's fingerprints  shall be forwarded to the Bureau of Criminal Identification and may be stored by electronic medium.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-608(5): 26B-6-201 HIV testing shall be conducted on a minor who is taken into custody after having been adjudicated for a sexual offense under Title 76, Chapter 5, Part 4, Sexual Offenses, upon the request of:

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-608(6)(b): in which:

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-609 Restraint of a minor.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-609(1): As used in this section, "restrained" means the use of handcuffs, chains, shackles, zip ties, irons, straightjackets, and any other device or method that is  used to immobilize a minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-609(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-609(2)(a): The Judicial Council shall adopt rules that address the circumstances under which a minor  may be restrained while appearing in juvenile  court.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-609(2)(b): The Judicial Council shall ensure that the rules consider both the welfare of the minor  and the safety of the juvenile  court.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-609(2)(c): A minor  may not be restrained during a juvenile  court proceeding unless restraint is authorized by rules of the Judicial Council.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-610 Property damage caused by a minor -- Liability of parent or guardian.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-610(1): A parent or guardian with legal custody of a minor is liable for damages sustained to property not to exceed $2,000 when:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-610(1)(a): the minor intentionally damages, defaces, destroys, or takes the property of another;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-610(1)(b): the minor recklessly or willfully shoots or propels a missile, or other object at or against a motor vehicle, bus, airplane, boat, locomotive, train, railway car, or caboose, whether moving or standing; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-610(1)(c): the minor intentionally and unlawfully tampers with the property of another and thereby recklessly endangers human life or recklessly causes or threatens a substantial interruption or impairment of any public utility service.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-610(2): (1); 76-9-802 A parent or guardian with legal custody of a minor is liable for damages sustained to property not to exceed $5,000 when the minor is adjudicated for an offense under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-610(2)(a): 76-9-802 for the benefit of, at the direction of, or in association with any criminal street gang as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-610(2)(b): to gain recognition, acceptance, membership, or increased status with a criminal street gang.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-610(3): (1); (2) A juvenile court may make an order for restitution under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-610(4): (1)(a); (c); (2); 76-6-101 As used in this section, property damage described under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-610(5): A court may waive part or all of the liability for damages under this section by the minor's parent or guardian if, after the minor is adjudicated, the court finds, upon the record:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-610(5)(a): good cause; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-610(5)(b): the parent or guardian:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-610(5)(b)(i): made a reasonable effort to restrain the wrongful conduct; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-610(5)(b)(ii): reported the conduct to the property owner involved or the law enforcement agency having primary jurisdiction after the parent or guardian knew of the minor's unlawful act.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-610(6): (5)(b) A report is not required under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-610(7): 76-6-106; 76-6-106.1; 76-6-206; 80-6-701; (1); (2) A conviction for criminal mischief under Section
