Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704 Detention or alternative to detention -- Limitations.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(1): 80-6-701; 78A-6-353; 78A-6-353
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(1)(a): 80-6-701; 78A-6-353 The juvenile court may order a minor to detention, or an alternative to detention, if the minor is adjudicated for:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(1)(a)(i): 80-6-701 an offense under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(1)(a)(ii): 78A-6-353 contempt of court under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(1)(b): 78A-6-353 Except as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(1)(c): If a minor is held in detention before an adjudication, the time spent in detention before the adjudication shall be credited toward the 30 cumulative days eligible as a disposition under Subsection (1)(b).
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(1)(d): If a minor spent more than 30 days in detention before a disposition, the juvenile court may not order the minor to detention under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(2): An order for detention under Subsection (1) may not be suspended upon conditions ordered by the juvenile court.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(3): 78A-6-353 A juvenile court may not order a minor to detention for:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(3)(a): 78A-6-353 contempt of court, except to the extent permitted under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(3)(b): a violation of probation;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(3)(c): failure to pay a fine, fee, restitution, or other financial obligation;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(3)(d): unfinished compensatory or community service hours;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(3)(e): an infraction; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(3)(f): a status offense.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(4): A juvenile court may not order a minor be placed in a correctional facility that is intended to hold adults accused or convicted of offenses as an alternative to detention under Subsection (1).
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(5)(a): If a minor is held in detention under this section, the minor is eligible to receive credit for good behavior against the period of detention.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(5)(b): The rate of credit is one day of credit for good behavior for every three days spent in detention.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(6): 80-6-703
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(6)(a): A minor may not be held in secure detention following a disposition by the juvenile court:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(6)(a)(i): under Chapter 3, Abuse, Neglect, and Dependency Proceedings; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(6)(a)(ii): except as provided in Subsection (6)(b), for a community-based program.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(6)(b): 80-6-703 If a minor is awaiting placement by the division under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(6)(c): The period of detention under Subsection (6)(b) may be extended by the juvenile court for a cumulative total of seven calendar days if:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(6)(c)(i): the division, or another agency responsible for placement, files a written petition with the juvenile court requesting the extension and setting forth good cause; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(6)(c)(ii): the juvenile court enters a written finding that it is in the best interests of both the minor and the community to extend the period of detention.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(6)(d): The juvenile court may extend the period of detention beyond the seven calendar days if the juvenile court finds, by clear and convincing evidence, that:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(6)(d)(i): the division, or another agency responsible for placement, does not have space for the minor; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(6)(d)(ii): the safety of the minor and community requires an extension of the period of detention.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(6)(e): The division, or the agency with custody of the minor, shall report to the juvenile court every 48 hours, excluding weekends and holidays, regarding whether the division, or another agency responsible for placement, has space for the minor.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(6)(f): The division, or agency, requesting an extension shall promptly notify the detention facility that a written petition has been filed.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-704(6)(g): The juvenile court shall promptly notify the detention facility regarding the juvenile court's initial disposition and any ruling on a petition for an extension, whether granted or denied.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-712(1): 80-6-702 If the juvenile court places a minor on probation under Section

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-712(2)(a)(ii): for aftercare services if the minor was placed out of the home, a period of supervision from three to four months, but may not exceed four months.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-712(2)(b): A minor may be supervised for aftercare services under Subsection (2)(a)(ii):
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-712(2)(b)(i): in the home of a qualifying relative or guardian;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-712(2)(b)(ii): at an independent living program contracted or operated by the division; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-712(2)(b)(iii): in a family-based setting with approval by the director or the director's designee if the minor does not qualify for an independent living program due to age, disability, or another reason or the minor cannot be placed with a qualifying relative or guardian.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-805 Parole procedures -- Conditions of parole.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-805(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-805(1)(a): A juvenile offender shall be served with notice of parole hearings and has the right to personally appear before the authority for parole consideration.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-805(1)(b): An order or decision of the authority shall be in writing.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-805(1)(c): A juvenile offender shall be provided written notice of the authority's reasoning and decision in  the juvenile offender's  case.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-805(2): 80-6-804 A juvenile offender may be paroled to the juvenile offender's home, to an independent living program contracted or operated by the division, to an approved independent living setting, or to other appropriate residences of qualifying relatives or guardians, but shall remain on parole until parole is terminated by the authority in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-805(3): (3)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-805(3)(a): Any condition of parole shall be specified in writing, and agreed to, by the juvenile offender.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-805(3)(b): (3)(a) An agreement under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-805(4): The authority may require a juvenile offender to pay restitution ordered by the juvenile court as a condition of release, placement, or parole.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806 Parole revocation -- Hearing -- Procedures.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(1)(a): The authority may only revoke the parole of a juvenile offender after a hearing and upon determination that there has been a violation of law or of a condition of parole by the juvenile offender that warrants the juvenile offender's return to secure care.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(1)(b): The parole revocation hearing shall be held at the secure care facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(2)(a): Before returning a juvenile offender to secure care for a parole revocation or rescission hearing, the division shall provide a prerevocation or prerescission hearing within the vicinity of the alleged violation, to determine whether there is probable cause to believe that the juvenile offender violated the conditions of the juvenile offender's parole.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(2)(b): Upon a finding of probable cause, the juvenile offender may be remanded to secure care, pending a revocation hearing.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(3): 80-6-607 The authority shall only proceed with the parole revocation or rescission process in accordance with the system of appropriate responses developed in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(4): A paroled juvenile offender is entitled to legal representation at the parole revocation hearing, and if the juvenile offender or the juvenile offender's family has requested but cannot afford legal representation, the authority shall appoint legal counsel.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(5)(a): A juvenile offender:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(5)(a)(i): shall receive timely advance notice of the date, time, place, and reason for the hearing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(5)(a)(ii): has the right to appear at the hearing.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(5)(b): The authority shall provide the juvenile offender an opportunity to be heard, to present witnesses and evidence, and to confront and cross-examine adverse witnesses, unless there is good cause for disallowing that confrontation.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(6): Decisions in parole revocation or rescission hearings shall be reached by a majority vote of the present members of the authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(7): 80-6-607; (7)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(7)(a): 80-6-607 The authority may issue a warrant to order any peace officer or division employee to take into custody a juvenile offender alleged to be in violation of parole conditions in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(7)(b): The division may issue a warrant to any peace officer or division employee to retake a juvenile offender who has escaped from secure care.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-806(7)(c): (7) Based upon the warrant issued under this Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-807 Discharge of juvenile offender.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-807(1): A juvenile offender may be discharged from the jurisdiction of the division at any time, by written order of the authority, upon a finding that no further purpose would be served by secure care or supervision in a community setting.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-807(2): 80-6-804 A juvenile offender shall be discharged in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-807(3): Discharge of a juvenile offender is a complete release of all penalties incurred by adjudication of the offense for which the juvenile offender was committed to secure care.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-808 Appeal regarding parole release or revocation.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-808(1): A juvenile offender, or the parent or guardian of a juvenile offender, may appeal to the executive director of the department, or the executive director's designee, any decision of the authority regarding parole release, rescission, or revocation.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-808(2): The executive director, or the executive director's designee, may set aside or remand the authority's decision only if the authority's decision is arbitrary, capricious, an abuse of discretion, or contrary to law.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901(1): "Adult" means an individual who is 18 years old or older.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901(2)(a): "Gang activity" means any criminal activity that is conducted as part of an organized youth gang.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901(2)(b): "Gang activity" includes any criminal activity that is done in concert with other gang members, or done alone if the criminal activity is to fulfill gang purposes.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901(2)(c): "Gang activity" does not include graffiti.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901(3): "Minor" means an individual who is:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901(3)(a): under 18 years old; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901(3)(b): 18 years old and still attending high school.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901(4)(a): "Minor offense" means any unlawful act that is a status offense or an offense that would be a misdemeanor, infraction, or violation of a municipal or county ordinance if committed by an adult.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901(4)(b): "Minor offense" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901(4)(b)(i): a class A misdemeanor; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901(4)(b)(ii): a felony of any degree.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901(5): "Sponsoring entity" means any political subdivision of the state, including a school or school district, juvenile court, law enforcement agency, prosecutor's office, county, city, or town.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901(6): "Status offense" means a violation of the law that would not be a violation but for the age of the offender.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901(7): "Youth court" means a diversion program that is an alternative disposition for cases involving minors who have committed minor offenses.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-901(8): 80-6-907(1) "Youth Court Board" means the board created under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902 Youth court -- Authorization -- Referral.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(1): 53G-8-211 A minor may serve in a youth court, under the supervision of an adult coordinator, in various capacities within the courtroom, acting in the role of jurors, lawyers, bailiffs, clerks, and judges.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(1)(a): 53G-8-211 A minor who appears before a youth court has been identified by law enforcement personnel, school officials, a prosecuting attorney, or the juvenile court as having committed an act, including a minor offense or eligible offense under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(1)(b): A youth court may only hear cases as provided for in this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(1)(c): A youth court is not a court established under the Utah Constitution, Article VIII.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(2): A youth court may not accept referrals from law enforcement, schools, prosecuting attorneys, or a juvenile court unless the youth court is certified by the Youth Court Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(3): 53G-8-211
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(3)(a): 53G-8-211 Any person may refer a minor to a youth court for a minor offense or for any other eligible offense under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(3)(b): Once a referral is made, the case shall be screened by an adult coordinator to determine whether the minor offense or other eligible offense qualifies as a youth court case.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(4): 53G-8-211 A youth court has authority over a minor:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(4)(a): 53G-8-211 referred for one or more minor offenses or who are referred for other eligible offenses under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(4)(b): who, along with a parent, guardian, or custodian, voluntarily and in writing, request youth court involvement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(4)(c): who, along with a parent, guardian, or custodian, agree to follow the youth court's disposition of the case.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(5): (6); 53G-8-211; (5)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(5)(a): (6); 53G-8-211 Except with permission granted under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(5)(b): (5)(a) Notwithstanding Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(6): (5) A youth court may exercise authority over a minor described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(7): Permission of the juvenile court may be granted by a juvenile probation officer in the district that would have jurisdiction over the offense being referred to a youth court.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(8): A youth court may:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(8)(a): decline to accept a minor for youth court disposition for any reason; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(8)(b): terminate a youth from youth court participation at any time.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(9): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(9)(a): A minor, or the minor's parent, guardian, or custodian may withdraw from the youth court process at any time.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(9)(b): The youth court shall immediately notify the referring source of the withdrawal.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(10): The youth court may transfer a case back to the referring source for alternative handling at any time.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(11): Referral of a case to youth court may not, if otherwise eligible, prohibit the subsequent referral of the case to any court.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(12): Proceedings and dispositions of a youth court may only be shared with the referring agency, juvenile court, and victim.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-902(13): When a minor does not complete the terms ordered by a youth court, and if the case is referred to a juvenile court, the youth court shall provide the case file to the juvenile court.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-903 Parental involvement -- Victims -- Restitution.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-903(1): A minor appearing before the youth court shall be accompanied by a parent, guardian, or custodian.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-903(2): A victim shall have the right to attend hearings and be heard.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-903(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-903(3)(a): Any restitution due to a victim of an offense shall be made in full prior to the time the case is completed by the youth court.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-903(3)(b): Restitution shall be agreed upon between the minor and the victim.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904 Dispositions.
--------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904(1): A youth court may order a disposition for:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904(1)(a): compensatory service;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904(1)(b): participation in law-related educational classes, appropriate counseling, treatment, or other educational programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904(1)(c): providing periodic reports to the youth court;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904(1)(d): participating in mentoring programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904(1)(e): participation by the minor as a member of a youth court;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904(1)(f): letters of apology;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904(1)(g): essays; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904(1)(h): any other disposition considered appropriate by the youth court and adult coordinator.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904(2): A youth court may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904(2)(a): impose a term of imprisonment or detention; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904(2)(b): impose fines.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904(3): A disposition by a youth court shall be completed within 180 days from the date of referral.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904(4): A disposition by a youth court shall be reduced to writing and signed by the minor and the minor's parent, guardian, or custodian indicating acceptance of the terms of the disposition.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904(5)(a): A youth court shall notify the referring source if a minor fails to successfully complete the youth court's disposition.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-904(5)(b): The referring source may then take any action the referring source considers appropriate.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-905 Liability.
-----------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-905(1): A person associated with the referral, evaluation, adjudication, disposition, or supervision of matters under this part may not be held civilly liable for any injury occurring to a minor performing compensatory service or any other activity associated with a certified youth court, unless the person causing the injury acted in a willful or wanton manner.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-905(2): A person participating in a certified youth court shall be considered  a volunteer for purposes of Workers' Compensation and other risk-related issues.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-906 Fees.
------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-906(1): (1); (1)
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-906(1)(a): A youth court may require that a minor pay a reasonable fee, not to exceed $50, to participate in the youth court.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-906(1)(b): (1) A fee under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-906(1)(c): (1) A fee under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-906(1)(d): Any fees collected shall be used for supplies and any training requirements.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-906(2): A minor who participates in youth court is responsible for the all expenses of any classes, counseling, treatment, or other educational programs that are the disposition of the youth court.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907 Youth Court Board -- Membership -- Responsibilities.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(1): The Youth Court Board shall be comprised of the following members:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(1)(a): the Utah attorney general or the attorney general's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(1)(b): one prosecuting attorney appointed by the Utah Prosecution Council;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(1)(c): one criminal defense attorney appointed by the Utah Association of Criminal Defense Attorneys;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(1)(d): one juvenile court judge appointed by the Board of Juvenile Court Judges;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(1)(e): the juvenile court administrator or the administrator's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(1)(f): the executive director of the commission or the executive director's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(1)(g): the state superintendent of education or the state superintendent's designee;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(1)(h): two representatives, appointed by the Utah Youth Court Association, from youth courts based primarily in schools;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(1)(i): two representatives, appointed by the Utah Youth Court Association, from youth courts based primarily in communities;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(1)(j): one member from the law enforcement community appointed by the Youth Court Board;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(1)(k): one member from the community at large appointed by the Youth Court Board; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(1)(l): the president of the Utah Youth Court Association.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(2): The Office of the Attorney General shall provide staff support and assistance to the Youth Court Board.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(3): (1)(a); (g); (1)(h); (k) The members selected to fill the positions in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(4): (1)(b); (c); (d); (j); (k); (1)(h); (i) Members shall serve two-year staggered terms beginning July 1, 2012, except the initial terms of the members designated by Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(5): The Youth Court Board shall meet at least quarterly to:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(5)(a): set minimum standards for the establishment of a youth court, including an application process, membership and training requirements, and the qualifications for the adult coordinator;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(5)(b): review certification applications; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(5)(c): provide for a process to recertify each youth court every three years.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(6): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (4) In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(7): The Youth Court Board may deny certification, recertification, or withdraw the certification of any youth court for failure to comply with program requirements.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(8): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-907(9): The Youth Court Board shall provide a list of certified youth courts to the Board of Juvenile Court Judges, all law enforcement agencies in the state, all school districts, and the Utah Prosecution Council by October 1 of each year.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-908 Establishing a youth court -- Sponsoring entity responsibilities.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-908(1): A youth court may be established by a sponsoring entity or by a private nonprofit entity that contracts with a sponsoring entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-908(2): The sponsoring entity shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-908(2)(a): oversee the formation of the youth court;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-908(2)(b): provide assistance with the application for certification from the Youth Court Board; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-908(2)(c): provide assistance for the training of youth court members.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-909 School credit.
---------------------------------------------
A local school board may provide school credit for participation to a member of a youth court.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001(5): "Petitioner" means an individual requesting an expungement or vacatur under this part.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001(1): "Abstract" means a copy or summary of a court's disposition.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001(2): 53E-1-102
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001(2)(a): "Agency" means a state, county, or local government entity that generates or maintains records for which expungement may be ordered under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001(2)(b): 53E-1-102 "Agency" includes a local education agency, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001(3)(a): "Expunge" means to remove a juvenile record from public inspection by:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001(3)(a)(i): sealing the juvenile record; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001(3)(a)(ii): restricting or denying access to the juvenile record.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001(3)(b): "Expunge" does not include the destruction of a juvenile record.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001(4)(a): "Juvenile record" means all records for all incidents of delinquency involving an individual that are in the custody of the juvenile court or an agency.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001(4)(b): "Juvenile record" does not include a record of an adjudication under Chapter 3, Abuse, Neglect, and Dependency Proceedings, or Chapter 4, Termination and Restoration of Parental Rights.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001(5): "Petitioner" means an individual requesting an expungement or vacatur under this part.


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001.1 Court records -- Abstracts.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001.1(1): A court or agency with custody of an individual's record related to an offense that the individual is alleged to have committed, or an offense that the individual committed, before the individual was 18 years old may not disclose the record to a federal agency that is responsible for criminal justice research or proceedings unless the court or the agency is required to share the record under state or federal law.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001.1(2): 53-3-218 An abstract of a record for a minor's adjudication of a traffic offense shall be submitted to the Department of Public Safety as provided in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001.2 Venue for petition seeking expungement.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Notwithstanding SectionUtah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001.2(1): in the court where the petition for delinquency was filed; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1001.2(2): if a petition for delinquency was never filed, in the juvenile court in the county in which the arrest occurred or the citation was issued.

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1004.5(1)(d): all nonjudicial adjustments were completed on or after October 1, 2023.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1004.5(2): 41-6a-502; 76-5-112; 76-5-206; 76-9-702.1; 76-10-505.5; 76-10-509.4 An individual's juvenile record is not eligible for expungement under Subsection (1) if the individual's juvenile record contains a nonjudicial adjustment for a violation of:

Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1006.1(4)(b): Within 60 days after the day on which an agency receives a copy of an expungement order, the agency shall mail an affidavit to the individual who is the subject of the expungement order, or the individual's attorney, that the agency has complied with the expungement order.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1006.1(5): 80-6-608 Notwithstanding Subsection (4), the Board of Pardons and Parole and the Department of Corrections:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1006.1(5)(a): may not disclose records expunged in an expungement order unless required by law;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1006.1(5)(b): 80-6-608 are not required to destroy any photograph or record created under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1006.1(5)(c): may use an expunged record for purposes related to incarceration and supervision of an individual under the jurisdiction of the Board of Pardons and Parole, including for the purpose of making decisions about:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1006.1(5)(c)(i): the treatment and programming of the individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1006.1(5)(c)(ii): housing of the individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1006.1(5)(c)(iii): applicable guidelines regarding the individual; or
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1006.1(5)(c)(iv): supervision conditions for the individual;
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1006.1(5)(d): are not prohibited from disclosing or sharing any information in an expunged record with another agency that uses the same record management system as the Board of Pardons and Parole or the Department of Corrections; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1006.1(5)(e): are not required to mail an affidavit under Subsection (4)(b).
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1006.1(6): Upon entry of an expungement order:
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1006.1(6)(a): an adjudication, a nonjudicial adjustment, a petition, an arrest, an investigation, or a detention for which the record is expunged is considered to have never occurred; and
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1006.1(6)(b): the individual, who is the subject of the expungement order, may reply to an inquiry on the matter as though there never was an adjudication, a nonjudicial adjustment, a petition, an arrest, an investigation, or a detention.
Utah Code Annotated § 80-6-1006.1(7): 80-6-1004.1; 80-6-1004.2; 80-6-1004.3; 80-6-1004.4; 80-6-1004.5 A record expunged under Section
